Permissibility of Ijtihad in the Prophet's Era
Discusses the permissibility of ijtihad in the Prophet's era

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the main positions on the permissibility of ijtihad during the Prophet's lifetime and identify the Hanafi preferred view.

Core Idea
Ijtihad was permissible in the Prophet's era, but when direct questioning is possible, it is preferable to seek his guidance.

A classical debate in usul al-fiqh asks whether a companion could engage in ijtihad while the Prophet (peace be upon him) was alive. This lesson lays out the spectrum of opinions—from absolute prohibition to absolute permission—and explains the reasoning behind the majority (Hanafi) position, which allows ijtihad conditionally.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main issue
The passage begins with an analogy from Prophet Ibrahim's dream interpretation to show that even prophets can err in non-revelatory matters, setting the stage for the permissibility of ijtihad.
This analogy is used to counter objections that ijtihad might lead to error.
2
List the schools on permissibility
Three views: absolute prohibition, absolute permission (majority), and conditional permission (for absent judges or with explicit permission). Note the nuance in each.
The text uses terms like 'مطلقاً' (absolutely) and 'بشرط غيبته للقضاء' (conditional on absence for judgment).
3
Examine the occurrence question
After establishing permissibility, the passage discusses whether ijtihad actually occurred. Four sub-views are mentioned: occurred absolutely (as supposition), never occurred, occurred only for absent persons, and suspension.
The author notes that al-Subki said no one claimed definitive occurrence.
4
Analyze the Hanafi position
The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that ijtihad is permissible absolutely, but when the Prophet is present and accessible, one should not resort to ijtihad without necessity or permission.
This is derived from the story of Mu'adh and the Banu Qurayza incident (detailed in the next lesson).

خاتمة في الاجتهاد والتقليد
من سيدهم الذي كان نبياً وآدم بين الماء والطين صلوات الله وسلامه عليه وآله الطاهرين وأصحابه المعظمين فأي استبعاد في وقوع الخطأ لإبراهيم عليه السلام في تعبير رؤياه التي رأى فيها أنه يذبح ابنه بل أمر في المنام بذبح الكبش ورآه مذبوحاً لكن في صورة الولد فلم يعبره وزعم أنه مأمور بذبح الولد، والدليل أنه رأى فيها أنه يذبحه، كما قال: ﴿إِنِّي أَرَى في الْمَنَاءِ أَنِّي أَذْبَحُكَ فَانظُرْ مَاذَا تَرَى [الصافات: ١٠٢] فلو لم تكن الرؤيا معبراً لوقع ذبح ابنه أو تكون كاذبة، وكلاهما باطلان فمن شنع على الشيخ الأكبر صاحب فصوص الحكم في تجويزه. هذا النحو من الخطأ فمن قلة تدبره وسوء فهمه وإنما شنع على نفسه وصار بحيث يضحك من صنعه هذا الصبيان فافهم وتثبت .
منهم
(مسألة : قالت طائفة : لا يجوز اجتهاد غيره في عصره عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام ومختار الأكثر الجواز (مطلقاً غيبة وحضوراً (وقيل) الجواز (بشرط غيبته للقضاء) لا لغيره بقصة معاذ بن جبل رضي الله عنه ( وقيل : (بالإذن يجوز (وإذا جاز ففي الوقوع مذاهب) الأول (نعم) واقع (مطلقاً) حضرة وغيبة لكن ظناً قال السبكي : لم يقل أحد أنه وقع قطعاً. كذا في «الحاشية» (واختاره الآمدي وابن الحاجب) والثاني (لا) يقع (وعليه الجبائي وابنه من المعتزلة على المشهور و الثالث (نعم) وقع في الغائب بقصة معاذ بن جبل رحمه الله تعالى، وقد مر، ولأنه قال حين توجه إلى بني قريظة : لا يصلين أحد العصر إلا في بني قريظة» فأدرك بعضهم العصر في الطريق، فقال بعضهم لا نصلي حتى نأتيها، وقال بعضهم : بل نصلي لم يرد منا ذلك، فذكر ذلك للنبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، فلم يعنف واحداً . رواه البخاري عن ابن عمر وفي رواية محمد بن إسحاق فأتى رجال من بعد العشاء الأخيرة، ولم يصلوا العصر لقول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم: «لا يصلين أحد إلا في بني قريظة فشغلهم أمر لم يكن منه بد وأبوا أن يصلوا لقول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم حتى أتوا بني قريظة فصلوا العصر بها بعد العشاء الأخيرة، فما عابهم الله بذلك في كتابه ولا عنفهم به رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وقال : حدث بهذا الحديث أبو إسحق بن يسار عن معبد بن كعب بن مالك الأنصاري (دون الحاضر) الذي يمكن له السؤال منه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وعليه الأكثر، و) الرابع (الوقف مطلقاً) حضرة وغيبة (وقيل) الوقف إلا فيمن غاب وعليه عبد الجبار) المعتزلي ( وكثير) الظاهر أنه تفسير للقول بالوقف والحق أن ترك اليقين إلى محتمل الخطأ مختاراً مما يأباه العقل فلا يعتبر بالقياس والاجتهاد عند إمكان السؤال ( ومن ثمة كانوا يرجعون إليه) صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم (إلا) لضرورة مانعة عن السؤال ( كالغائب البعيد) فإنه لا يقدر على السؤال قبل فوت الحادثة (أو) للإذن من الرسول صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم بالحكم فإن الرغبة عما أذن به إلى غيره ،حرام، لأن الإصابة حينئذ مقطوعة (كتحكيم سعد بن في بني قريظة) حين حاصرهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم ونزلوا على حكم سعد بن معاذ (فحكم بقتلهم وسبى ذراريهم فقال عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة معاذ
Chapter on Ijtihad and Taqlid: From their master who was a prophet while Adam was between water and clay, may prayers and peace be upon him and his pure family and honored companions. So what improbability is there in the occurrence of error to Ibrahim (peace be upon him) in interpreting his dream in which he saw that he was slaughtering his son? Rather, he was commanded in the dream to slaughter the ram and saw it slaughtered, but in the form of the son, so he did not interpret it and thought he was commanded to slaughter the son. The evidence is that he saw in it that he was slaughtering him, as He said: {Indeed, I have seen in a dream that I am slaughtering you, so see what you think} [as-Saffat:102]. If the dream were not interpretable, then either the slaughter of his son would have occurred or it would be false, and both are invalid. So whoever criticizes the greatest shaykh, author of Fusus al-Hikam, for permitting this type of error, it is due to his lack of reflection and poor understanding. Rather, he has criticized himself and become such that children laugh at his action. So understand and be steadfast. Among them: (Issue: A group said: Ijtihad by others is not permissible in his era, peace be upon him and his family and companions. The choice of the majority is permissibility, absolutely, whether the Prophet is absent or present. And it was said: permissibility is conditional on his absence for the purpose of judgment, not for other matters, based on the story of Mu'adh ibn Jabal, may Allah be pleased with him. And it was said: it is permissible with permission. If it is permissible, then regarding its actual occurrence there are schools. The first: Yes, it occurred absolutely, whether present or absent, but as a supposition. al-Subki said: No one said it occurred definitively. As in al-Hashiyah. And al-Amidi and Ibn al-Hajib chose it. The second: No, it did not occur, and upon this is al-Jubba'i and his son among the Mu'tazila according to the well-known view. The third: Yes, it occurred in the case of an absent person, based on the story of Mu'adh ibn Jabal, may Allah have mercy on him, which has passed. And because when he (the Prophet) headed towards Banu Qurayza, he said: 'Let no one pray Asr except in Banu Qurayza.' Some of them caught the Asr prayer on the way, and some said: We will not pray until we reach it, and some said: Rather we will pray; he did not intend that from us. So they mentioned that to the Prophet, may Allah bless him and his family and companions and grant them peace, and he did not rebuke any of them. Narrated by al-Bukhari from Ibn 'Umar. And in the narration of Muhammad ibn Ishaq: Some men came after the last Isha prayer and had not prayed Asr because of the saying of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and his family and companions and grant them peace: 'Let no one pray except in Banu Qurayza.' Their matter kept them busy and they refused to pray until they came to Banu Qurayza and prayed Asr there after the last Isha. Allah did not blame them for that in His Book, nor did the Messenger of Allah rebuke them for it. And he said: This hadith was narrated by Abu Ishaq ibn Yasar from Ma'bad ibn Ka'b ibn Malik al-Ansari. (The fourth opinion is: It is absolutely suspended, whether present or absent. And it was said: It is suspended except for one who is absent, and 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Mu'tazili and many others hold this. What is apparent is that this is an interpretation of the saying of suspension. The truth is that leaving certainty for what is possibly erroneous, willingly, is something that reason rejects, so analogy and ijtihad are not considered when questioning is possible. Hence they used to refer to him, peace be upon him and his family and companions, except for a necessity preventing questioning, like a distant absent person, for he cannot ask before the incident passes, or because of permission from the Messenger to rule, for desiring what he has permitted over something else is forbidden, because correctness then is certain – like the arbitration of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh in the matter of Banu Qurayza when the Messenger laid siege to them and they surrendered to the judgment of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh, and he judged that their men be killed and their children taken captive. So he, peace be upon him and his family and companions, said: 'You have judged with the judgment of Allah.' In another wording from al-Bukhari, he said: 'You have decreed with the decree of Allah.'
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the permissibility and actual occurrence of ijtihad during the lifetime of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). It begins with an analogy to Prophet Ibrahim's error in interpreting his dream, to show that even prophets can err in non-revelatory matters. The main issue is: can a companion engage in ijtihad while the Prophet is alive and accessible? A minority said no; the majority said yes, either absolutely or with conditions (prophet's absence or permission). Then it discusses whether such ijtihad actually occurred. Three positions: (1) it occurred absolutely but only as a supposition (never certain), (2) it never occurred, (3) it occurred only in the case of an absent person, citing the story of Mu'adh. The story of the companions delaying Asr prayer until reaching Banu Qurayza is cited as evidence for the permissibility of ijtihad in the Prophet's absence, as they interpreted his order differently and the Prophet did not rebuke them. The fourth opinion is that the matter is suspended; but the correct view is that when questioning the Prophet is possible, one cannot leave certainty for probability. Exceptions are distant absence or the Prophet's explicit permission to rule by ijtihad, like Sa'd ibn Mu'adh's judgment. The passage emphasizes that the Prophet's actions and approvals demonstrate the validity of ijtihad under those conditions.

Key Terms
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihad): Exertion of effort by a qualified scholar to derive a ruling when no explicit text or consensus is available.
التقليد (al-taqlid): Following a mujtahid without demanding proof; contrasted with ijtihad.
التقرير (al-taqrir): The Prophet's tacit approval of a statement or action by remaining silent when aware of it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following represents the view of the majority (الأكثر) on the permissibility of ijtihad during the Prophet's era?
A) It is absolutely prohibited.
B) It is permissible absolutely, whether the Prophet is present or absent.
C) It is only permissible if the Prophet is absent for judgment.
D) It is permissible only if the Prophet explicitly permits it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position holds that ijtihad was permissible during the Prophet's lifetime, but when direct access to him was possible, seeking his guidance was preferable except for necessity or permission.

Ijtihad — Independent Reasoning

Evidence for Occurrence: The Banu Qurayza Incident
Provides the detailed hadith evidence and exceptions for ijtihad during the Prophet's era

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the Banu Qurayza hadith as evidence for ijtihad in the Prophet's absence and explain the exceptions to the rule.

Core Idea
The Prophet's lack of rebuke in the Banu Qurayza incident proves the validity of ijtihad when direct consultation is impossible or permitted.

The Banu Qurayza incident is a cornerstone evidence for those who argue that ijtihad occurred during the Prophet's time. This lesson unpacks the hadith, its implications, and how later Hanafis used it to justify ijtihad in cases of necessity, absence, or explicit permission.

Guided Path
1
Read the incident details
The hadith narrates that the Prophet ordered the companions to pray Asr only in Banu Qurayza. Some prayed on the way, others delayed until reaching the location. Neither group was rebuked.
Two versions: one from Bukhari (summary), one from Muhammad ibn Ishaq (detailed).
2
Identify the proof structure
The Prophet's silence (sukut) after being informed of the differing interpretations is taken as taqrir (tacit approval). This is a primary source in Hanafi usul.
Taqrir is a form of sunnah; it indicates that the action is acceptable.
3
Understand the exceptions
The passage then states a general principle: leaving certainty for probability is rationally unacceptable. Therefore, ijtihad is only permissible when questioning the Prophet is impossible (e.g., distance) or when he explicitly permits it (e.g., Sa'd's arbitration).
This qualifies the absolute permission mentioned earlier.
4
Apply to the fourth opinion
The fourth opinion (suspension) is explained as actually meaning that ijtihad is not allowed when questioning is possible. Thus, the evidence supports conditional ijtihad.
The author considers this the correct view ('الحق').

Source Text

Chapter on Ijtihad and Taqlid: From their master who was a prophet while Adam was between water and clay, may prayers and peace be upon him and his pure family and honored companions. So what improbability is there in the occurrence of error to Ibrahim (peace be upon him) in interpreting his dream in which he saw that he was slaughtering his son? Rather, he has criticized himself and become such that children laugh at his action. So understand and be steadfast. Among them: (Issue: A group said: Ijtihad by others is not permissible in his era, peace be upon him and his family and companions. The choice of the majority is permissibility, absolutely, whether the Prophet is absent or present. And it was said: permissibility is conditional on his absence for the purpose of judgment, not for other matters, based on the story of Mu'adh ibn Jabal, may Allah be pleased with him. And it was said: it is permissible with permission. If it is permissible, then regarding its actual occurrence there are schools. The first: Yes, it occurred absolutely, whether present or absent, but as a supposition. al-Subki said: No one said it occurred definitively. As in al-Hashiyah. And al-Amidi and Ibn al-Hajib chose it. The second: No, it did not occur, and upon this is al-Jubba'i and his son among the Mu'tazila according to the well-known view. The third: Yes, it occurred in the case of an absent person, based on the story of Mu'adh ibn Jabal, may Allah have mercy on him, which has passed. And because when he (the Prophet) headed towards Banu Qurayza, he said: 'Let no one pray Asr except in Banu Qurayza.' Some of them caught the Asr prayer on the way, and some said: We will not pray until we reach it, and some said: Rather we will pray; he did not intend that from us. So they mentioned that to the Prophet, may Allah bless him and his family and companions and grant them peace, and he did not rebuke any of them. Narrated by al-Bukhari from Ibn 'Umar. And in the narration of Muhammad ibn Ishaq: Some men came after the last Isha prayer and had not prayed Asr because of the saying of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and his family and companions and grant them peace: 'Let no one pray except in Banu Qurayza.' Their matter kept them busy and they refused to pray until they came to Banu Qurayza and prayed Asr there after the last Isha. Allah did not blame them for that in His Book, nor did the Messenger of Allah rebuke them for it. And he said: This hadith was narrated by Abu Ishaq ibn Yasar from Ma'bad ibn Ka'b ibn Malik al-Ansari. (The fourth opinion is: It is absolutely suspended, whether present or absent. And it was said: It is suspended except for one who is absent, and 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Mu'tazili and many others hold this. What is apparent is that this is an interpretation of the saying of suspension. The truth is that leaving certainty for what is possibly erroneous, willingly, is something that reason rejects, so analogy and ijtihad are not considered when questioning is possible. Hence they used to refer to him, peace be upon him and his family and companions, except for a necessity preventing questioning, like a distant absent person, for he cannot ask before the incident passes, or because of permission from the Messenger to rule, for desiring what he has permitted over something else is forbidden, because correctness then is certain – like the arbitration of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh in the matter of Banu Qurayza when the Messenger laid siege to them and they surrendered to the judgment of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh, and he judged that their men be killed and their children taken captive. So he, peace be upon him and his family and companions, said: 'You have judged with the judgment of Allah.' In another wording from al-Bukhari, he said: 'You have decreed with the decree of Allah.'
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the permissibility and actual occurrence of ijtihad during the lifetime of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). It begins with an analogy to Prophet Ibrahim's error in interpreting his dream, to show that even prophets can err in non-revelatory matters. The main issue is: can a companion engage in ijtihad while the Prophet is alive and accessible? A minority said no; the majority said yes, either absolutely or with conditions (prophet's absence or permission). Then it discusses whether such ijtihad actually occurred. Three positions: (1) it occurred absolutely but only as a supposition (never certain), (2) it never occurred, (3) it occurred only in the case of an absent person, citing the story of Mu'adh. The story of the companions delaying Asr prayer until reaching Banu Qurayza is cited as evidence for the permissibility of ijtihad in the Prophet's absence, as they interpreted his order differently and the Prophet did not rebuke them. The fourth opinion is that the matter is suspended; but the correct view is that when questioning the Prophet is possible, one cannot leave certainty for probability. Exceptions are distant absence or the Prophet's explicit permission to rule by ijtihad, like Sa'd ibn Mu'adh's judgment. The passage emphasizes that the Prophet's actions and approvals demonstrate the validity of ijtihad under those conditions.

Key Terms
التقرير (al-taqrir): The Prophet's tacit approval of a statement or action by remaining silent when aware of it.
الوقف (al-waqf): Suspension of judgment; in this context, suspending a ruling on whether ijtihad occurred.
التحكيم (al-tahkim): Arbitration; refers to the Prophet delegating judgment to Sa'd ibn Mu'adh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following exceptions allows ijtihad even when the Prophet is alive?
A) When the mujtahid is more knowledgeable than other companions
B) When the Prophet is absent (distant) or has given explicit permission
C) When the issue is about warfare
D) When the companion is a close relative of the Prophet

Key Takeaway
The Banu Qurayza incident, combined with the Sa'd arbitration, provides strong evidence that ijtihad was valid during the Prophet's lifetime but only under the conditions of necessity or explicit permission.

Rulings on the Mistaken Mujtahid in Rational and Shar'i Matters
Defining rulings for correct and mistaken mujtahids

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between definitive and theoretical matters in ijtihad and state the Hanafi ruling for the mistaken mujtahid in each category.

Core Idea
Error in definitive matters (rational or shar'i) leads to sin or disbelief; error in theoretical matters leads only to sin.

This passage from 'Fawatih al-Rahamut' lays out the Hanafi taxonomy of ijtihad errors. It clarifies when a mujtahid's mistake is excusable, when it is merely sinful, and when it amounts to disbelief. The discussion also engages with the Mu'tazili view that absolves the mistaken mujtahid of all sin.

Guided Path
1
Name the two main categories
Identify the two broad domains of ijtihad: rational ('aqliyyat) and shar'i (shar'iyyat). Note that both have definitive (qat'i) and non-definitive (nazari) subcategories.
2
State the ruling for rational errors
For rational matters: if the error denies the religion of Islam, the mujtahid is a disbeliever and sinful; if it does not (e.g., saying the Quran is created), he is only sinful, not a disbeliever.
Abu Hanifa's statement about 'kufr ni'mah' is key.
3
Apply the same structure to shar'i matters
For shar'i matters: denying definitive rulings (pillars, Quranic authority) makes one a disbeliever; denying theoretical rulings (ijma', khabar wahid, qiyas) makes one sinful but not a disbeliever.
Definitive here means no possibility of contrary even remotely.
4
Compare with al-Jahiz's view
Al-Jahiz (Mu'tazili) holds that the mistaken mujtahid is not sinful at all, even if he incurs the worldly judgment of disbelief. The Hanafi rejection is based on the clarity of definitive proofs.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf in usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خطأ
الله
(مسألة: المصيب) من المجتهدين أي الباذلين جهدهم في العقليات واحد: وإلا اجتمع النقيضان لكون كل من القدم والحدوث مثلاً مطابقاً للواقع وخلاف العنبري المعتزلي فيه بظاهره غیر معقول) بل بتأويل كما سيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى (والمخطىء فيها) أي في العقليات (إن كان نافياً لملة الإسلام فكافر وآثم على اختلاف في شرائطه كما مر) من بلوغ الدعوة عند الأشعرية ومختار المصنف ومضي مدة التأمل والتمييز عند أكثر الماتردية (وإن لم يكن) نافياً لملة الإسلام كخلق) (القرآن أي القول به ونفي الرؤية والميزان. وأمثال ذلك (فآثم لا كافر، ومن ثمة أي من أجل أنه عند مشايخنا غير كافر أوّلوا ما روي (عن) الإمام (الشافعي) رضي الله عنه مثل ما روي عن الإمام أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه (من تكفير قائله) في أصول الإمام فخر الإسلام. قول أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه : من قال بخلق القرآن فهو كافر بالله بكفران النعمة) حيث أبى على المنعم ما ليس هو أهله والشرعيات القطعيات كذلك) أي مثل العقليات فمنكر الضروريات الدينية ( منها كالأركان الأربعة التي بنى الإسلام عليها الصلاة والزكاة والصوم والحج (وحجية القرآن ونحوهما كافر آثم، ومنكر النظريات) منها (كحجية الإجماع وخبر الواحد وعدوّا منها حجية القياس أيضاً (آثم فقط) غير كافر، والمراد بالقطع المعنى الأخص ، وهو ما لا يحتمل النقيض ولو احتمالاً بعيداً، ولو غير ناشيء عن الدليل (وقال) أبو مسلم (الجاحظ) المعتزلي (لا إثم على المجتهد المخطىء) الباذل جهده في طلب الحق أصلاً وإن جرى عليه في الدنيا حكم الكفر) لنفيه ملة الإسلام (بخلاف) الكافر (المعاند) الذي يعلم الحقية ثم ينكر عناداً كاليهود وكفار قريش، وكذا من لم يجتهد لمعرفة الحق (وقيل: هو مراد العنبري بقوله : كل مجتهد ولو في العقليات مصيب، قال التفتازاني : إنه أراد من لا يكون نافياً لملة ،الإسلام بل كان من أهل القبلة وكيف يدعي من ينتمي إلى الإسلام
(Issue: The correct one) among the mujtahids, i.e., those who exert their utmost effort, in rational matters is one; otherwise two opposites would coexist, since each of eternity and origination, for example, corresponds to reality. The contrary view of al-Anbari al-Mu'tazili on it, taken literally, is unreasonable, but rather by interpretation, as will come, Allah willing. (And the mistaken one in them) i.e., in rational matters (if he is a denier of the religion of Islam, then he is a disbeliever and sinful, with a difference in its conditions, as passed) regarding the reaching of the call according to the Ash'aris and the author's choice, and the passing of a period of reflection and distinction according to most Maturidis. (And if he is not) a denier of the religion of Islam, like (saying) (the creation of the Quran), i.e., the statement of it, and denial of the vision (of Allah) and the Scale and the like, (then he is sinful, not a disbeliever. Hence, i.e., because according to our scholars he is not a disbeliever, they interpreted what was narrated (from) Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him, similar to what was narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, regarding declaring its speaker a disbeliever) in the Usul of Imam Fakhr al-Islam. The saying of Abu Hanifa: 'Whoever says the Quran is created is a disbeliever in Allah with the disbelief of ingratitude for grace,' because he refused to the Giver what is not appropriate for Him. (And the definite matters of Sharia are likewise) i.e., like rational matters. So whoever denies the religious necessities (such as the four pillars upon which Islam is built: prayer, zakat, fasting, and Hajj, and the authority of the Quran and the like, is a disbeliever and sinful. And whoever denies the theoretical matters (such as the authority of consensus and the solitary report, and they include the authority of analogy as well, is only sinful, not a disbeliever. And what is meant by definite is the more specific meaning, which is that which does not admit of contradiction even remotely, even if not arising from evidence. (And said) Abu Muslim al-Jahiz al-Mu'tazili: (There is no sin on the mistaken mujtahid) who exerts his effort in seeking the truth at all, even if the judgment of disbelief is passed on him in this world) due to his denial of the religion of Islam, unlike the obstinate disbeliever who knows the truth and then denies out of obstinacy, like the Jews and the disbelievers of Quraysh, and likewise one who does not exert effort to know the truth. (And it was said: That is what al-Anbari meant by his saying: Every mujtahid, even in rational matters, is correct. al-Taftazani said: He meant one who does not deny the religion of Islam, rather is among the people of the qibla. How can one who claims to belong to Islam...
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage defines the categories of 'correct' (musib) and 'mistaken' (mukhti') among mujtahids, focusing on rational ('aqli) and shar'i matters. In rational matters (like the createdness of the Quran, vision of Allah), only one view is correct; the opposite is false. A mujtahid who errs in a rational matter and as a result denies the religion of Islam (e.g., by denying the existence of God) becomes a disbeliever. If his error does not negate Islam (e.g., saying the Quran is created, denying ru'ya, mizan) he is sinful but not a disbeliever, according to Hanafi scholars. The text mentions that Imam Abu Hanifa called the one who says the Quran is created a 'disbeliever in Allah with kufr ni'mah' (ingratitude), not outright apostasy. In shar'i matters, denying definitive rulings (like the five pillars, authority of Quran) makes one a disbeliever and sinful; denying theoretical matters (like consensus, solitary hadith, analogy) only makes one sinful, not a disbeliever. The passage also discusses al-Jahiz's view that there is no sin on the mistaken mujtahid, and it reconciles al-Anbari's statement that every mujtahid is correct, explaining it as meant only for those who do not deny the fundamentals of Islam.

Key Terms
العقليات (al-'aqliyyat): Matters known through rational proofs, such as the existence of God, attributes, etc.
الشرعيات القطعيات (al-shar'iyyat al-qat'iyyat): Definitive shar'i matters, like the obligation of the five pillars, known with certainty from the Quran and mutawatir sunnah.
النظريات (al-nazariyyat): Theoretical matters in Sharia, like the authority of ijma' and khabar wahid, derived through ijtihad.
المصيب (al-musib): The mujtahid whose ijtihad arrives at the correct ruling (in rational matters, only one).
المخطئ (al-mukhti'): The mujtahid whose ijtihad yields an incorrect ruling.
كفران النعمة (kufr al-ni'mah): Disbelief of ingratitude; a lesser form of disbelief that does not remove one from Islam entirely, used by Abu Hanifa for the one who says the Quran is created.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, what is the ruling on a mujtahid who denies the authority of consensus (ijma')?
A) He becomes a disbeliever and sinful.
B) He is only sinful, not a disbeliever.
C) He is neither sinful nor a disbeliever.
D) He is considered correct in his ijtihad.

Key Takeaway
The severity of an error in ijtihad depends on whether the matter is rationally definitive, shar'i definitive, or theoretical — only definitive errors may lead to disbelief.

The Mistaken Mujtahid in Speculative Matters
Rule: No sin on mistaken mujtahid in dhanniyat unless following desire

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a mistaken mujtahid is not sinful in speculative matters and apply the distinction between following desire and legitimate ijtihad.

Core Idea
No sin on a mistaken mujtahid in speculative matters unless he follows his desire.

This lesson examines the Hanafi principle that a mujtahid who errs in a speculative (dhanni) matter is not sinful, provided he exerted his full effort and did not follow his personal desire. The passage addresses a subtle objection: what if the matter is definitive but contains a remote possibility? We'll unpack the reasoning and see how the rule applies to judicial rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and conditions
Locate the key phrase: 'speculative matters' (dhanniyat) and the condition 'if he exerted all effort' (ijtahada kulla al-juhd).
2
Analyze the objection and response
Read the objection: 'Your definition includes definitive matters with a remote possibility.' Then follow the author's response: the mujtahid no longer sees it as definitive; thus no sin.
3
Distinguish sin from legal validity
Note that absence of sin does not mean the ruling is correct; it may be overturned by another judge who sees it as definitively invalid.
4
Apply the exception of desire (hawa)
Identify that following desire (hawa) makes the mujtahid sinful, even if he claims ijtihad. This is a key boundary.
5
Summarize the rule and its implications
State the rule: in speculative matters, a mistaken mujtahid is not sinful if he exerted full effort and did not follow desire, but his ruling may be overturned by another judge.
This rule protects sincere ijtihad while allowing correction of manifest error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الظنيات المعلومة ظناً بالمعنى الأعم الذي فيه احتمال الخلاف ولو بعيداً غير ناشيء عن دليل (فلا إثم على المخطىء فيها إذا اجتهد كل الجهد فأدى رأيه إلى الاحتمال البعيد، فأول النص إلى ذلك الاحتمال فإن قلت : قد شمل الظني بتفسيرك القاطع الذي فيه احتمال غير ناشيء عن دليل وخلافه باطل قطعاً حتى ينقض القضاء به، فكيف يصح عدم الإثم؟ قلت : هذا القاطع يحتمل الخلاف في كونه قطعاً، ولما أدى اجتهاده إلى الاحتمال البعيد صار قريباً في ظنه فلم يبق قاطعاً فلا يأثم إلا إذا دعاه الهوى إلى ذلك الاحتمال، وحينئذ نحن نقول بالإثم قطعاً، وأما نقض القضاء فلكونه مقطوعاً عند قاض ناقض مبتلی به فصار عنده باطلاً بيقين فينقض هذا غاية الكلام فافهم
As for speculative matters known by conjecture in the broader sense, which contains the possibility of disagreement even if remote, and not arising from evidence, there is no sin on the mistaken one in them if he exerted all effort, and his opinion led to the remote probability. He interpreted the text according to that probability. If you say: Your interpretation of the speculative has included the definitive that contains a possibility not arising from evidence, and its opposite is definitively invalid, even to the point that a judicial ruling based on it would be overturned. So how can there be no sin? I say: This definitive [matter] contains the possibility of it not being definitive [in the mind of the mujtahid]. And when his ijtihad led to the remote probability, it became close in his estimation, so it no longer remains definitive. So he is not sinful unless his desire called him to that probability. In that case, we say he is definitely sinful. As for overturning the judicial ruling, it is because it is definitive for the overturning judge who is faced with it, so he considers it definitely invalid, so he overturns. This is the end of the discussion. Understand.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage establishes the Hanafi rule regarding speculative matters (dhanniyat). The term 'speculative' is defined as matters known by conjecture in the broader sense, which includes the possibility of a remote counterview not arising from a formal proof. In such matters, if a mujtahid exerts his full effort and his ijtihad leads to a remote probability, he is not sinful for his error. The text addresses an objection: that this definition includes definitive matters that have a remote possibility (which is not based on evidence), such that the opposite is known to be invalid, as when a judge's ruling based on such a matter must be overturned. The response explains that if the mujtahid's ijtihad leads him to the remote probability, he no longer considers it definitive; thus he is not sinful, unless he followed his desire. However, the judicial ruling may still be overturned by another judge who considers it definitively invalid. This shows that the absence of sin does not prevent the correction of a ruling based on a different ijtihad.

Key Terms
ظنيات (dhanniyat): Speculative matters; issues where the evidence yields conjecture, not certainty, and admits the possibility of a remote counterview not arising from a formal proof.
هوى (hawa): Desire or caprice that leads a person away from following the correct evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is a mujtahid not sinful for his error in a speculative matter?
A) When he follows his desire
B) When he exerts full effort and his ijtihad leads to a remote probability
C) When he ignores the text
D) When he follows a definitive proof

Key Takeaway
In speculative matters, a mujtahid who exerts full effort and does not follow desire is not sinful for his error, though his ruling may be overturned by another judge.

The Debate on Taswib: Is Every Mujtahid Correct?
Presenting the dispute on whether every mujtahid is musib or only one is correct

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether every mujtahid is correct, identify the opposing view (taswib), and explain the Hanafi dalil from the Sahaba's practice of declaring ijtihad errors.

Core Idea
Truth is one; the mujtahid who hits it gets two rewards, the one who misses gets one.

This lesson examines a foundational usul dispute: Is every mujtahid correct (musib) or is only one correct? The Hanafi school holds that there is a single divine ruling for each ijtihadi matter, and the mujtahid who hits it is rewarded doubly; the one who misses is rewarded once for his effort. Opponents argue that ijtihadi matters have no predetermined ruling—the ruling is what the mujtahid concludes. We will analyze the evidence and practical consequences of this difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The debate centers on whether for every ijtihadi matter (a topic open to ijtihad) there is a specific divine ruling that the mujtahid aims to discover, or whether the ruling is whatever the mujtahid's ijtihad yields.
Note the distinction between 'truth is one' and 'truth is many'.
2
State the opposing view (taswib) and its proponents
The taswib view holds that every mujtahid is correct in his ruling. This is attributed to Qadi Abu Bakr, al-Ash'ari (with weak chain), al-Ghazali, al-Muzani, and some Mu'tazila like al-Jubba'i. They argue there is no predetermined divine ruling; the ruling becomes divine when the mujtahid reaches it.
Note the caveat: attribution to al-Ash'ari is disputed by Khurasanis.
3
State the Hanafi view
The Hanafi (and the four imams) hold that there is one specific divine ruling for each action, established by a proof (dalil). The mujtahid who hits that ruling is correct (musib) and gets two rewards; the one who misses is not correct but is rewarded for his ijtihad effort (one reward). This is the meaning of 'every mujtahid is correct' according to Abu Hanifa: correct in effort, but truth is one.
The term 'musib' has two levels: hit the truth (reality) vs. rewarded for correct effort.
4
Analyze the Hanafi dalil from Sahaba practice
The author argues that the Sahaba frequently declared other mujtahids mistaken, e.g., they declared Ibn 'Abbas mistaken for not adopting 'awl (proportional increase) in inheritance. This shows they believed error is possible, so truth is one. Even though Hanafis deny 'awl, the example demonstrates the principle that the Sahaba recognized error in ijtihad.
The dalil is qawl sahabi (sayings of the Companions), transmitted widely, giving experiential certainty (qati thubut, though dalala is zanni).
5
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If every mujtahid were correct, then contradictory rulings (like the amount of head to wipe in wudu: Hanafi quarter, Shafi'i three hairs, Maliki all) would all be true in reality, which is impossible. The Hanafi view avoids this by affirming one actual truth while rewarding all sincere mujtahids.
This shows why the dispute matters for fatwa and coexistence of schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: كل مجتهد في المسألة الاجتهادية) أي فيما يسوغ فيه الاجتهاد (مصيب عند القاضي أبي بكر (و) الشيخ (الأشعري) كما قال أهل العراق وقال أهل خراسان: لم يثبت عن الأشعري، كذا في الحاشية ونسب إلى الإمام حجة الإسلام (الغزالي) قدس سره (والمزني) من كبار أصحاب الشافعي رضي الله عنه (وغيرهما) ولا يذهب عليك ما في القول من الإشارة إلى ضعف هذه النسبة فلا تفعل، وهؤلاء ظنوا أن لا حكم الله تعالى في تلك الواقعات. إلا أنه إذا وصل رأي المجتهد إلى أمر فهو الحكم عند الله تعالى (ولا ينافي) هذا (قدم الكلام) كما ظن زعماً منه بأن قدمه يوجب قدم الحكم كقدم العلم) أي كما لا ينافي قدم العلم حدوث المعلوم، وذلك لأن الكلام وإن كان قديماً لكن التعلقات بحدوث الاجتهادات فافهم. وبعض منهم قالوا الحكم من الأزل هو ما أدى إليه رأي المجتهد (وعليه الجبائي) من المعتزلة ونسبته إلى جميع المعتزلة لم تصح كيف والحسن أو القبح عندهم في مرتبة الذات) فما فيه حسن واقعي هو الواجب لا يمكن أن يكون محرماً، وما فيه القبح الواقعي فهو محرم لا غير، ولا ينقلب الحسن والقبح الذاتيان. وإذا كان كل مجتهد مصيباً (فالحق عندهم متعدد) فعلى كل من أدى اجتهاده إلى حكم فهو الحكم، وإذا أدى رأي آخر إلى آخر فهو الحكم عليه، فعلى الحنفية الفرض مسح ربع الرأس في الواقع، وعلى الشافعي ثلاث شعرات، وعلى المالكية مسح كل الرأس ولكن اختلفوا في أن تلك الحقوق متساوية كما هو الظاهر على ذلك التقدير (أو أحدها أحق وهو القول بالأشبه المنسوب إلى بعضهم (والمختار أن الله حكماً معيناً) في أفعال العباد أوجب طلبه ونصب عليه دليلاً لا كما زعم البعض أنه لم ينصب عليه دليلاً، وإنما يصل إليه العبد بالاتفاق المحض، ثم هذا الدليل ظني عند الأكثر قطعي عند من تقدم فمن أصابه فله أجران أجر الاجتهاد وأجر الإصابة، ولا وجه لهذا الأجر إلا الرحمة الإلهية، لأنّ إصابته ليست بفعل مقدور إنما المقدور له بذل الجهد فإن اتفق تأدى نظره إلى مقدمات مناسبة له أصابه، لكن النص دل على أن له أجرين فيجب القبول ومن أخطأه فله أجر) واحد (لامتثاله أمر الاجتهاد ببذل الوسع ولا أجر بمقابلة الخطأ، فإن الخطأ وإن لم يكن مؤاخذاً به، إلا أنه لا الأجر عليه وهذا معنى قول الحنفية أن المجتهد (المخطىء مصيب) ابتداء، أي مأجور بفعله ومخطىء انتهاء (وهذا) أي كون الحق واحداً (هو الصحيح عند الأئمة الأربعة وعبر عنه الإمام أبو حنيفة رحمه الله فقال : كل مجتهد مصيب، والحق عند الله تعالى واحد يعني مصيب في بذل وسعه حتى يؤجر عليه، والحق عند الله واحد قد يصيبه وقد لا (واعلم أن النزاع المذكور إنما هو (في الفقهيات المتعلقة بالأعمال (فلا يتوجه إليه (أن) قولنا ليس كل مجتهد مصيباً صواب أو خطأ، وعلى التقديرين لا إيجاب كلياً أما على الأوّل فظاهر، وأما على الثاني فهذا خطأ (۲) فالمجتهد الواصل نظره إليه على خطأ فثبت المدعي ووجه عدم التوجه ظاهر لنا أوّلاً: إطلاق الصحابة كثيراً الخطأ في الاجتهاد ولم ينكر) وتكرر بحيث حدث علم بالتجربة أن الكل كانوا متفقين عليه فخطأوا ابن عباس في عدم القول بالعول، وهو خطأهم، فقال: من شاء باهلته، إنّ الله لم يجعل في مال نصفاً ونصفاً وثلثاً) هذا اللفظ في كتب الفرائض، ورواه سعيد بن منصور عن ابن عباس قال : أترون الذي أحصى رمل عالج عدداً، جعل في المال نصفاً وثلثاً وربعاً، إنما هو نصفان وثلاثة أثلاث وأربعة أرباع، وقد عرفت أن الحنفية ينكرونه ويقولون فيه انقطاع باطن، ثم إنّ هذا القول بعيد منه أيضاً
Issue: Every mujtahid in an ijtihadi matter — i.e., in what is permissible for ijtihad — is correct (musib) according to Qadi Abu Bakr and Shaykh al-Ash'ari, as the people of Iraq said, while the people of Khurasan said it is not established from al-Ash'ari. Likewise in the gloss, it is attributed to Imam Hujjat al-Islam al-Ghazali, may God sanctify him, and al-Muzani, among the major associates of al-Shafi'i, may God be pleased with him, and others. And do not overlook what is in the statement indicating the weakness of this attribution, so do not do it. These thought that there is no ruling of God in those occurrences. However, when the opinion of the mujtahid reaches something, then it is the ruling according to God, and this does not contradict the pre-eternity of the Speech, as they imagined, claiming that its pre-eternity necessitates the pre-eternity of the ruling like the pre-eternity of knowledge — i.e., just as pre-eternity of knowledge does not contradict the occurrence of the known. That is because Speech, though pre-eternal, its relations occur with the occurrence of ijtihads, so understand. Some of them said that the ruling from eternity is what the mujtahid's opinion leads to, and upon this is al-Jubba'i of the Mu'tazila, but its attribution to all Mu'tazila is not correct, because for them good and evil are in the essence themselves. So what has real good is obligatory and cannot be forbidden, and what has real evil is forbidden exclusively, and the essential good and evil do not change. And if every mujtahid is correct, then according to them truth is multiple. So upon each one whose ijtihad leads to a ruling, it is the ruling, and if another opinion leads to another, it is the ruling upon that. For Hanafis, the obligatory is wiping a quarter of the head in reality; for Shafi'i, three hairs; for Malikis, wiping the entire head. But they differed as to whether these truths are equal, as is apparent on that estimation, or one of them is more worthy — that is the view of the 'ashbah' attributed to some. And the chosen view is that God has a specific ruling in the actions of servants, which He made obligatory to seek and established a proof for it, not as some claimed that He did not establish a proof, and that the servant reaches it by pure chance. Then this proof is speculative according to most, definitive according to those before. So one who hits it has two rewards: the reward of ijtihad and the reward of correctness. There is no basis for this reward except divine mercy, because his correctness is not a volitional act; the only volitional act is exerting effort. So if it happens that his consideration leads to suitable premises, he hits it. But the text indicates he has two rewards, so it must be accepted. And one who misses it has one reward, for complying with the command of ijtihad by exerting capacity. There is no reward corresponding to the error, for error, even if not punishable, receives no reward. This is the meaning of the Hanafi statement: the mistaken mujtahid is correct initially — i.e., rewarded for his action — and mistaken finally. And this — that truth is one — is the correct view according to the four imams, and Imam Abu Hanifa, may God have mercy on him, expressed it by saying: 'Every mujtahid is correct, but the truth with God is one.' He meant correct in exerting his capacity so that he is rewarded for it, but the truth with God is one; he may hit it or not. And know that the mentioned dispute is only in fiqh matters related to actions. So it is not addressed by the statement: 'Our saying that not every mujtahid is correct is either correct or wrong; in either case it is not universally binding.' For on the first it is obvious, and on the second this is an error. So the mujtahid who reaches his opinion to it is in error, so the claim is established. The reason for not addressing is apparent to us: first, the Companions frequently declared error in ijtihad and it was not denied, and it was reiterated such that experiential knowledge arose that they all agreed upon it. So they declared Ibn 'Abbas mistaken for not adopting al-'awl, and they declared him mistaken. He said: 'Whoever wants, I will imprecate him; verily Allah has not made in wealth a half and a half and a third.' This wording is in the books of inheritance. And Sa'id ibn Mansur narrated from Ibn 'Abbas that he said: 'Do you think that He who counted the sand of 'Alij as a number has made in wealth a half, a third, and a quarter? It is only halves, three thirds, and four quarters.' And you know that the Hanafis deny it and say there is internal inconsistency in it. Then this saying is far from him as well.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage presents the well-known usul dispute (ikhtilaf) on whether every mujtahid is correct (musib) or only one is correct (al-musib wahid). The author attributes the 'taswib' view (every mujtahid correct) to Qadi Abu Bakr, al-Ash'ari (with a note of weak attribution), al-Ghazali, al-Muzani, and others. They argued that there is no predetermined divine ruling in ijtihadi matters; rather, the ruling is what the mujtahid's opinion reaches, and this does not contradict the pre-eternity of divine Speech because the rulings relate to the ijtihad. Some like al-Jubba'i said the ruling is from eternity what the mujtahid finds. The author rejects the extreme view leading to multiple truths (e.g., different valid rulings on wiping the head in wudu). The chosen (mukhtar) view is that there is a specific divine ruling in each case, established by a proof (dalil) that is either definitive or speculative. The mujtahid who hits it gets two rewards (for ijtihad and correctness), and the one who misses gets one reward (for ijtihad). This is the Hanafi position, expressed by Abu Hanifa: 'Every mujtahid is correct, but truth is one.' The correct is one, and the mujtahid is rewarded for his effort, not for the error. The author notes that the dispute only applies to furu' (fiqh matters), not usul. He presents the proof from the practice of the Sahaba: they often declared a mujtahid mistaken, e.g., Ibn 'Abbas for not adopting 'awl in inheritance—showing that they believed error is possible, so truth is one. The Hanafis deny 'awl, but the example still shows the principle. The commentary should highlight that the Hanafi position aligns with the four imams.

Key Terms
مصيب (musib): Correct: in the context of ijtihad, either meaning that the mujtahid is correct in his ruling (if truth is many) or that he is rewarded and his effort is correct (Hanafi view).
أجر (ajr): Reward: for the mujtahid, if correct he gets two rewards (for ijtihad and for hitting truth), if mistaken he gets one reward (for ijtihad).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this lesson, how many rewards does a mujtahid receive if he correctly identifies the actual divine ruling?
A) One reward for effort.
B) Two rewards: for ijtihad and for correctness.
C) Three rewards: for ijtihad, for hitting truth, and for teaching.
D) No reward, because correctness is expected.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position: there is one correct ruling for each ijtihadi matter; the mujtahid is rewarded for his effort, not for error.

Ijtihad — Independent Reasoning
advanced
8 min
Ijtihad: The Possibility of Error in the Mujtahid's Ruling
Argues for the Hanafi position that mujtahid can err

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the Hanafi proof that the mujtahid can err and refute the opposing view that every mujtahid is correct.

Core Idea
If the divine ruling followed the mujtahid's assumption, knowledge and assumption would combine—impossible.

The Hanafi school holds that a mujtahid may be correct or mistaken in his ruling. This lesson examines the rational proof for this position, responses from those who hold that every mujtahid is correct (musawwiba), and the Hanafi defense.

Guided Path
1
Define the mujtahid's object of pursuit
The mujtahid seeks an informative proposition (maṭlūb khabarī) that can be true or false. This sets up the possibility of error.
If the object were not informative but purely practical, error might not be definable.
2
State the Hanafi rational proof
If the divine ruling depended on the mujtahid's assumption (zann), then he would have both assumption and certainty at the same time, which is contradictory. Since retraction of rulings is accepted, assumption must remain alongside certainty.
The proof is presented as 'law kāna al-ḥukm al-ilāhī tābiʿan li-ẓannihī la-ijtamaʿa al-naqīḍān'.
3
Understand the first objection
Opponents claim the object of assumption is not the hukm itself but its appropriateness (alīqiyya) to principles; the hukm itself is known with certainty.
This objection attempts to separate the objects of zann and qat'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
Appropriateness is a necessary concomitant of being the hukm, so assumption of appropriateness still implies possible absence, coexisting with certainty of the hukm—a combination akin to contradictories.
The rebuttal shows the objection fails to avoid the contradiction.
5
Examine further objections and responses
The opponent analogizes the mujtahid to a prophet; the Hanafi response distinguishes certainty from zann from certainty from revelation, and explains that the first can be overridden.
This reinforces the Hanafi position that error is possible.

عهد من الشارع اعتباره وليس هذا أمراً فقهياً فأقول فيه إنه يجري الكلام في الأليقية فيجوز الخطأ فيها بل يقع لتخالف المجتهدين، فيكون بعض ما أدى إليه رأي مجتهد ليس أليق بما عهد من الشارع اعتبار، وهو حكم الله عندهم وحق (فيلزم على رأيهم أن بعض حكم الله تعالى في الواقع مما لا يليق بما عهد من الشارع اعتباره (في الواقع، وذلك باطل كما ترى فافهم). ولهم أن يقولوا في الجواب عن هذا أن المطلوب كونه حكم الله تعالى في حقي، وهو وإن كان بالنظر إلى نفس المفهوم قابلاً للصدق والكذب، إلا أن يكون صادقاً لكون حكم الله تعالى بحسب الظن فتدبر (واستدل) على المختار (أولاً) : لو كان الحكم الإلهي (تابعاً لظنه لاجتمع النقيضان، لأنه أي المجتهد (بظنه يقطع أنه حكم الله ، والظن باق كما كان من قبل (ضرورة، ولذا صح) له (الرجوع عنه . ولو لم يكن الظن باقياً بل صار مقطوعاً لما صح الرجوع، لأن المقطوع غير محل للاجتهاد والرجوع (فيكون عالماً به) أي بالحكم (حين كونه ظانا) به، فاجتمع الظن، ومع ،٤١٩ خاتمة في الاجتهاد والتقليد والعلم، وهو ملزوم اجتماع النقيضين ويرد عليه وجوه، أولها كما أقول: إن متعلق الظن ليس حكم الله أي ليس كونه حكم الله (بل) ما هو أليق بالأصول كما عرفت) والقطع يتعلق بكون حكم الله (فاختلف المتعلقان وفيه أنه من المستحيل أن يكون حكم من أحكام الله تعالى غير لائق بالأصول، فكونه أليق من لوازم كونه حكم الله تعالى فالظن به يستلزم احتمال انتفائه، هذا الاحتمال وجد القطع بكونه حكم الله تعالى وهو في قوّة اجتماع النقيضين فتدبر (وثانيها: أن المجتهد عندهم كنبي ذي شريعة في حق الحكم، فكما أن النبي يحكم بوحيه كذلك يحكم هو بظنه والظن كالوحي موجب للحكم قطعاً ما لم يثبت الرجوع الذي هو كالنسخ فلا بقاء للظن) حين وجود القطع بل إنما هناك الباقي القطع فقط) والظن كالعلة المعدة له وتجويز الرجوع لا يقدح فيه أي في القطع كتجويز (النسخ) فإنه لا يقدح فيه، ولك أن تقول : إنه قد وقع الإجماع على أن المقطوع لا يجوز فيه اجتهاد يوصل إلى نقيضه، فلو حدث ههنا يقين وقطع لما صح ،الرجوع، وكون الرجوع نسخاً إنما يكون إذا بقي مظنونية الحكم، اللهم إلا أن يفرق بين القطع الحاصل بتوسط الظن وبينه حاصلاً عن قاطع شرعي موجب للقطع ابتداء، ويجوز نقض الأوّل بالاجتهاد دون الثاني فافهم. (وبهذا) الجواب (اندفع ما قيل : لو كان الظن موجباً للعلم لامتنع ظن نقيضه مع تذكره لامتناع ظن نقيض ما علم يقيناً (مع تذكر الموجب للعلم لأن العلم لازم لموجبه بخلاف الأمارة إذ لا ربط عقلي) بين الأمارة وبين ما هي أمارة له . .. وجه الدفع أن الرجوع من علم إلى علم آخر متعلق بنقيضه، كالرجوع من العلم الحاصل بالمنسوخ إلى الحاصل بالناسخ والسر فيه أن الحاصل بعد الظن علم لا يحتمل الخلاف من البدء، ولكن يحتمل الارتفاع بالرفع الطارىء، فبقاؤه مظنون، فيحتمل تبدله بمبدل هو الظن بنقيضه وثالثها: أنه مشترك الإلزام (للإجماع بيننا وبينكم على وجوب اتباع الظن قطعاً، فاجتمعا أيضاً ويدفع بأن محل الظن عندنا هو حكمه تعالى، ومحل العلم حرمة مخالفة ما أدّى إليه رأيه ما دام على ظنه فاختلف المتعلقان فلا استحالة (إن قيل) إذا أجبتم بهذا فيمكن الجواب لهم عن دليلكم بأن متعلق الظن كون الدليل دليلاً، ومتعلق العلم ثبوت (مدلوله الذي هو حكم الله تعالى ( ما دام (دليلا فاختلف المتعلقان أيضاً (أجيب) عنه (كما في المختصر بأن كونه دليلاً حكم شرعي أيضاً وإن كان غير عملي، فإذا ظنه) دليلاً (فقد علمه وإلا يعلمه بل احتمل أنه ليس دليلاً في الواقع لجاز التعبد بغيره) في الواقع، فلم يبق الحكم المدلول متيقناً، بل جاز التعبد بضدّه المدلول الدليل آخر، فقد لزم العلم بكون الدليل دليلاً، وقد فرضتم مظنوناً، هذا خلف وفيه أن العلم بالمدلول إنما فرعوه على الظن بالحكم فقط) بأن جعلوه كالمعد (من غير ادعاء العلم بدليله كيف ولم يقولوا بحصول العلم بالحكم بهذا الدليل حتى يجب علمه (وجواز التعبد بغيره ما دام مظنوناً ممنوع) فإنّ التعبد بالمظنون لا غير، وإنما الجواز بعد بطلان ،ظنه ولا استحالة فيه. فإنه حينئذ يبطل بمدلوله بمنزلة مجيء الناسخ (مع أن كونه أي الدليل دليلاً عقلياً) ليس شرعياً أصلاً (نعم: وجوب العمل بمقتضاه شرعي واعلم أن هذا غير ضار للمختصر، فإنه وإن كان عقلياً يجب قطعيته وإلا احتمل
Because the proponents of 'awl do not say this, but rather they say: since Allah did not make half, third, and quarter at all, and allocated shares in this manner, it is known that these are shares for each when alone, and when together each decreases proportionally to their shares. Then what is narrated from him that he gives precedence to the preferred and wastes the rest. If what is meant by 'preferred' in inheritance when conflicting, it is unknown, and it is also not intended. And if 'preferred' means the two spouses and the mother, and 'deferred' means the sisters and daughters, as in the narration of al-Bayhaqi and al-Hakim, then it is pure caprice; entitlement is for all equally by text. Then the concealment of children and siblings by spouses is something reason abhors. The truth is that Ibn Abbas is innocent of such statements. From that is the statement of the best of the truthful after the prophets, peace be upon them, and upon Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him, regarding al-kalala: 'I say by my opinion, if it is correct it is from Allah, and if it is wrong it is from Satan' — its chain is not known. Similarly, the statement of Ibn Mas'ud regarding al-mufawwada has preceded, but the word 'error' is only in what is transmitted from books of usul. And from that is the statement of the Commander of the Faithful Ali to the Commander of the Faithful Umar, may Allah honor their faces, regarding al-mujahhidah — with damma on the mim and kasra on the ha — which is the woman who came to the Commander of the Faithful and miscarried. He said to Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf: 'What do you say?' He said: 'You are only a teacher, no blame on you.' So he asked the Commander of the Faithful Ali, and he said: 'If he exercised ijtihad and erred, and if he did not exercise ijtihad he betrayed you, I see upon you a blood-money of a slave or a slave-girl.' The pronoun is for Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf in the narration of al-Bayhaqi. That is in al-Taqrir. And what is in Sharh al-Sharh and others: 'if they both exercised ijtihad' — in the dual form, the pronoun for both Uthman and Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf — this is not established. And for us: secondly: The mujtahid is a seeker of an informative sought-object for which he investigates, and it admits of correctness and error. If it is [objectively] matching and he reaches it, he is correct; otherwise he is wrong, as in intellectual matters. The response that his sought-object is what is predominant in his opinion from the evidence, whatever it is, does not help to refute this, because the assumption (zann) that comes from evidence pertains only to the ratio that conveys the ruling, absolutely. So there must be an informative sought-object subject to truth and falsehood. Thus error is found in one who does not reach it. And what is in Sharh al-Mukhtasar that that ratio is not a predicate in the sense of being the hukm of Allah, but rather it is the most appropriate to what is known from the Lawgiver to be considered — and this is not a fiqh matter. So I say about it: speech is about appropriateness, so error is permissible in it, rather it occurs, due to the disagreement of mujtahids. Thus some of what the opinion of a mujtahid leads to is not the most appropriate to what is known from the Lawgiver to be considered, yet it is the hukm of Allah according to them and true. So it follows from their view that some of the hukm of Allah in reality is not appropriate to what is known from the Lawgiver to be considered — in reality, and that is false as you see, so understand. And they can say in response to this: the sought-object is its being the hukm of Allah in my right, and although it is, in terms of the concept itself, subject to truth and falsehood, yet it is true because the hukm of Allah is according to assumption (zann), so contemplate. And [the author] argued for the chosen position first: if the divine hukm were dependent on his assumption, two contradictories would combine, because he, i.e. the mujtahid, based on his assumption, becomes certain that it is the hukm of Allah, while the assumption remains as it was before, necessarily. Hence it is valid for him to retract it. If the assumption did not remain but became certain, retraction would not be valid, because the certain is not subject to ijtihad and retraction. So he would be knowing of it, i.e. of the hukm, at the time he is assuming it. Thus assumption and [page 419] knowledge combine, and this entails the combination of two contradictories. Several objections are raised against it. The first of them, as I say: The object of the assumption is not the hukm of Allah, i.e. not its being the hukm of Allah, but rather what is more appropriate to the principles, as you have known. And certainty pertains to its being the hukm of Allah. So the two objects differ. But it is said: It is impossible that a ruling from the rulings of Allah is not appropriate to the principles. So its being more appropriate is a necessary concomitant of its being the hukm of Allah. Thus assumption of it entails the possibility of its absence; this possibility coexists with certainty of its being the hukm of Allah, and this is in the strength of the combination of two contradictories, so contemplate. The second objection: That the mujtahid according to them is like a prophet having a law with respect to the ruling. Just as the prophet rules by his revelation, he rules by his assumption, and assumption like revelation necessitates the ruling definitively as long as retraction is not established, which is like abrogation. So there is no remaining of assumption at the time of certainty; rather only certainty remains. And assumption is like the preparatory cause for it, and the possibility of retraction does not vitiate it, i.e., vitiate the certainty, just as the possibility of abrogation does not vitiate it. But you may say: There is consensus that for what is certain, ijtihad leading to its opposite is not permissible. So if certainty and cutness occur here, retraction would not be valid. Retraction being abrogation only occurs if the ruling remains in the realm of assumption. Unless one distinguishes between certainty attained through assumption and certainty obtained from a shari‘ evidence that necessitates certainty from the outset. The first may be overridden by ijtihad, but not the second, so understand. With this response is refuted what is said: If assumption necessitated knowledge, it would be impossible to assume its opposite while remembering it, because it is impossible to assume the opposite of what is known with certainty, while remembering the cause of knowledge, because knowledge is necessary from its cause, unlike the indicator (amara) since there is no rational connection between the indicator and what it indicates. The manner of refutation is that retraction is from knowledge to another knowledge concerning its opposite, like retraction from the knowledge obtained from the abrogated to the knowledge obtained from the abrogating. The secret in it is that what is attained after assumption is knowledge that does not admit of disagreement from the beginning, but it admits of being raised by a supervening raising. So its continuation is assumed, so it may be replaced by a substitute that is the assumption of its opposite. The third objection: That it is a shared requirement, because there is consensus between us and you on the obligatory nature of following assumption definitively. So they also combine. And it is repelled by saying: The locus of assumption according to us is His hukm, and the locus of knowledge is the prohibition of contradicting what his opinion led to as long as he is on his assumption. So the two objects differ, so no impossibility. If it is said: If you respond with this, then they can answer your proof by saying: The object of assumption is that evidence is evidence, and the object of knowledge is the confirmation of its import, which is the hukm of Allah, as long as it is evidence. So the two objects also differ. The response to it is, as in al-Mukhtasar, that its being evidence is also a shar‘i ruling, even if it is not practical. So if he assumes it to be evidence, he knows it; otherwise he does not know it, but rather it is possible that it is not evidence in reality, then it would be permissible to worship by other than it in reality. So the ruling of the import does not remain certain, but rather it is possible to worship by its opposite imported by another evidence. Thus knowledge of the evidence being evidence is necessitated, yet you have assumed it — this is a contradiction. But it is said: Knowledge of the import is only derived from assumption of the ruling alone, by making it preparatory, without claiming knowledge of its evidence. How so? Since they did not claim attainment of knowledge of the ruling by this evidence such that its knowledge is necessary. And the permissibility of worship by other than it as long as it is assumed is denied, for worship is only by what is assumed, and permission only after its assumption is void, and no impossibility in that. For then its import is invalidated like the coming of an abrogator, although its being evidence is intellectual, not shar‘i at all. Yes: the obligation to act by its implication is shar‘i. Know that this does not harm al-Mukhtasar, for even if it is intellectual, its certainty is necessary, otherwise it would be probable.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage is a commentary in the Hanafi usul work Fawatih al-Rahmut, expanding on the topic of ijtihad and whether a mujtahid can be wrong in his ruling. The author argues for the Hanafi position that the mujtahid's ruling is not infallible and can be erroneous. 

The discussion begins with a critique of a reported view attributed to Ibn Abbas, but the author defends Ibn Abbas as being innocent of such statements. Then the author defines the mujtahid as a seeker of an informative object (matlub khabari) that admits of truth and falsehood. The opposing view is that the mujtahid's object is what is predominant in his opinion (mā yaghlubu ʿalā ẓannihī min al-dalīl). The author rejects this because the assumption (zann) derived from evidence relates only to the ratio that conveys the ruling, not to the ruling itself; thus there must be an informative object subject to truth and falsehood, and error can occur.

The author then presents a rational proof for the chosen position: if the divine ruling (al-hukm al-ilāhī) were dependent on the mujtahid's assumption, then two contradictories would combine. The mujtahid becomes certain that his assumption is the hukm of Allah, yet the assumption remains as it was (i.e., it is still zann, not certainty). If it had become certainty, retraction would not be valid, but retraction is valid, so assumption persists. Thus he is knowing and assuming at the same time, which is absurd. Responses to this proof are then examined. 

The first response says the object of assumption is not the hukm itself but its appropriateness (alīq) to the principles, while certainty pertains to its being the hukm. The author refutes this by noting that it is impossible for a ruling of Allah to be inappropriate to the principles, so appropriateness is a concomitant of being the hukm. Therefore assumption of appropriateness entails possible absence, coexisting with certainty of the hukm, which is like combining contradictories. 

The second response analogizes the mujtahid to a prophet; just as a prophet's revelation gives certainty, so too does the mujtahid's assumption—it becomes like revelation (ka-al-wahy) and necessitates the ruling definitively until abrogation. However, the author notes the consensus that certainty cannot be subject to new ijtihad, so if certainty arises, retraction is impossible. But the author resolves this by distinguishing between certainty obtained through assumption (which may be overridden) and certainty from a direct shari‘ evidence (which cannot). 

The third response argues that both sides agree on the obligation to follow assumption definitively, leading to a combination of differing loci. The author responds that the loci differ: assumption pertains to the hukm of Allah, while certainty pertains to the prohibition of contradicting that assumption as long as it persists. Then a counter-response is considered: that the object of assumption is the evidence being evidence, and the object of certainty is the import (the hukm). The author responds by arguing that if the evidence is assumed, it must be known; otherwise it could be invalid, leading to uncertainty. But the opponent might deny knowledge of the evidence, saying knowledge of the import is derived only from assumption of the ruling, not the evidence. The author denies that worship by another evidence is permissible while the assumption persists. 

Finally, the author notes that the evidence being evidence is intellectual, not shar‘i, but the obligation to act by it is shar‘i. This does not harm the position of al-Mukhtasar.

Key Terms
المجتهد (al-mujtahid): One who exerts himself to derive a legal ruling from the sources using his opinion (ra'y) and assumption (zann).
الظن (al-ẓann): A predominant probability (ghalabat al-ẓann) that is less than certainty; it is the basis for the mujtahid's ruling.
المطلوب الخبري (al-maṭlūb al-khabarī): An informative object that can be true or false, such as 'this is the hukm of Allah'.
الأليقية (al-alīqiyya): The attribute of being appropriate (alīq) to the principles (uṣūl) of the Shari'a.
النقيضان (al-naqīḍān): Two propositions that cannot both be true or both false, e.g., existence and non-existence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main rational proof presented in the passage for the Hanafi position that the mujtahid can be wrong?
A) If the divine ruling followed the mujtahid's assumption, then he would have both assumption and certainty simultaneously, which is absurd.
B) The mujtahid is like a prophet, so his assumption is like revelation.
C) The mujtahid's object is what is appropriate to the principles, not the hukm itself.
D) There is consensus that following assumption is obligatory definitively.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position that a mujtahid can err is established by the impossibility of combining assumption and certainty regarding the divine ruling.

Ijtihad — Independent Reasoning
advanced
12 min
Distinguishing Objects of Zann and Qat' in Taswib
Responding to objections by distinguishing objects of zann and qat'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi usul distinction between the objects of zann and qat' resolves the charge of contradictory beliefs in taswib.

Core Idea
Zann and qat' differ in object: zann targets 'most fitting', qat' targets 'being God's ruling' — no conjunction of opposites.

This passage defends the view that every mujtahid is correct (taswib). A key objection is that if zann (conjecture) leads to certainty (qat') about God's ruling, then the possibility of the opposite is impossible, yet it coexists — a contradiction. The Hanafi response hinges on distinguishing the objects: zann relates to what is 'most fitting to the principles', while qat' relates to 'its being God's ruling'. These are different loci, so the objection collapses.

Guided Path
1
State the first objection
Identify the critique that zann leading to qat' entails a conjunction of opposites because the possibility of error remains alongside certainty.
This is the 'conjunction of opposites' argument.
2
Extract the Hanafi response
Find the distinction: zann is about what is 'most fitting to the principles', qat' is about 'its being God's ruling'. These are different objects, so no contradiction.
The author adds that 'most fitting' is a necessary concomitant of 'being God's ruling', so the zann implies possibility, but qat' is about the necessary accompaniment.
3
Analyze the second objection (mujtahid-prophet analogy)
The opponent argues that if zann causes certainty, a mujtahid cannot change his ruling (like a prophet's revelation). The Hanafi response: the certainty from zann is not absolute; it can be reversed like abrogation.
Distinction: certainty from a definitive proof cannot be reversed, but certainty through zann can be overturned by new ijtihad.
4
Understand the third objection (consensus on following zann)
Opponent: consensus obligates following zann with certainty, creating a second conjunction. Response: the object of zann is the ruling itself, the object of knowledge is the prohibition of opposing it — different loci.
This maintains consistency: one's zann is about the ruling, while the certainty is about the obligation to act.

خاتمة في الاجتهاد والتقليد والعلم، وهو ملزوم اجتماع النقيضين ويرد عليه وجوه، أولها كما أقول: إن متعلق الظن ليس حكم الله أي ليس كونه حكم الله (بل) ما هو أليق بالأصول كما عرفت) والقطع يتعلق بكون حكم الله (فاختلف المتعلقان وفيه أنه من المستحيل أن يكون حكم من أحكام الله تعالى غير لائق بالأصول، فكونه أليق من لوازم كونه حكم الله تعالى فالظن به يستلزم احتمال انتفائه، هذا الاحتمال وجد القطع بكونه حكم الله تعالى وهو في قوّة اجتماع النقيضين فتدبر (وثانيها: أن المجتهد عندهم كنبي ذي شريعة في حق الحكم، فكما أن النبي يحكم بوحيه كذلك يحكم هو بظنه والظن كالوحي موجب للحكم قطعاً ما لم يثبت الرجوع الذي هو كالنسخ فلا بقاء للظن) حين وجود القطع بل إنما هناك الباقي القطع فقط) والظن كالعلة المعدة له وتجويز الرجوع لا يقدح فيه أي في القطع كتجويز (النسخ) فإنه لا يقدح فيه، ولك أن تقول : إنه قد وقع الإجماع على أن المقطوع لا يجوز فيه اجتهاد يوصل إلى نقيضه، فلو حدث ههنا يقين وقطع لما صح ،الرجوع، وكون الرجوع نسخاً إنما يكون إذا بقي مظنونية الحكم، اللهم إلا أن يفرق بين القطع الحاصل بتوسط الظن وبينه حاصلاً عن قاطع شرعي موجب للقطع ابتداء، ويجوز نقض الأوّل بالاجتهاد دون الثاني فافهم. (وبهذا) الجواب (اندفع ما قيل : لو كان الظن موجباً للعلم لامتنع ظن نقيضه مع تذكره لامتناع ظن نقيض ما علم يقيناً (مع تذكر الموجب للعلم لأن العلم لازم لموجبه بخلاف الأمارة إذ لا ربط عقلي) بين الأمارة وبين ما هي أمارة له . .. وجه الدفع أن الرجوع من علم إلى علم آخر متعلق بنقيضه، كالرجوع من العلم الحاصل بالمنسوخ إلى الحاصل بالناسخ والسر فيه أن الحاصل بعد الظن علم لا يحتمل الخلاف من البدء، ولكن يحتمل (مدلوله الذي هو حكم الله تعالى ( ما دام (دليلا فاختلف المتعلقان أيضاً (أجيب) عنه (كما في المختصر بأن كونه دليلاً حكم شرعي أيضاً وإن كان غير عملي، فإذا ظنه) دليلاً (فقد علمه وإلا يعلمه بل احتمل أنه ليس أفضى إلى القطع بالأعداء ولا استحالة إنما الاستحالة حصول القطع بالمدلول مع ظنية الدليل فافهم. (و) استدل على المختار :(ثانياً : إن تساوى (دليلاهما أي الاجتهادين المتخالفين تساقطا، فالحكم بالحقية تحكم ، وإلا فالصواب هو الراجح فلا حقية لكل (وأجيب بأن الرجحان) عندهم (تابع لظن المجتهد فيقول : كلاهما راجحان في ظن المجتهدين، فمدلولاهما مظنونان لهما، فهما حقان عليهما في نفس الأمر (أقول: على أن الخطأ الرجحان لا يستلزم الخطأ في الحكم فلا نسلم أن الصواب هو الراجح، (لأن الرجحان ولو ظنه غير مطابق للواقع يفضي إلى الظن، وهو إلى القطع، تدبر. و) استدل على المختار :(ثالثاً : أجمعوا على شرع المناظرة بين المجتهدين، وإنما فائدتها ظهور الصواب) فلو لم يحتمل كل مجتهد الخطأ لما كان لهذا الشرع المجمع عليه بعد علمهما بأن كليهما حكم (الله باجتهادهما فالاشتغال بها لذلك) الترجيح أو التساوي تحصيل الحاصل، فإنه لا مزيد عليه بعد الرجوع إلى الراجح أو إلى دليل آخر مغاير له، فإنه بعد هذا يحصل أيضاً حكم الله. وقبله كان كذلك، فلا فائدة في شرع المناظرة أصلاً (و) استدل على المختار رابعاً : يلزم على التصويب) لكل مجتهد (حل المجتهدة وحرمتها) معاً على بعلها (لو قال بعلها المجتهد : أنت بائن، ثم قال : راجعتك والرجل
