The Finality of Ijtihad-Based Rulings in Hanafi Usul
Rule on the finality of ijtihad rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that ijtihad-based court rulings are not overturned unless they contradict a qat'i proof, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a judge ruling against his own ijtihad.

Core Idea
Ijtihad rulings stand unless they clash with a definitive text; overturning them leads to endless litigation.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut addresses a foundational principle of judicial finality in Islamic law. It establishes that a judge's ijtihad-based ruling is final and cannot be overturned simply because another mujtahid disagrees. The only ground for overturning is a contradiction with a definitive proof (qat'i). The text also explores the consequence of infinite regress if overturning were allowed, and examines a specific case where a judge rules contrary to his own ijtihad, highlighting a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Main Rule
Read the opening statement: 'لا ينقض الحكم في الاجتهاديات إذا لم يخالف قاطعاً'. This is the core rule: ijtihad rulings are not overturned unless they contradict a definitive proof. Note what qualifies as qat'i: Qur'an, mutawatir sunna, mashhur sunna, and ijma.
This rule is a qa'ida usuliyya that preserves the finality of judgments.
2
Understand the Rationale
The text warns that if overturning were allowed, it would lead to an infinite regress (tasalsul), as a later ijtihad could overturn the first overturning, and so on. This would defeat the purpose of appointing a judge—to resolve disputes conclusively.
The rationale is based on maslaha (public interest) and sadd al-dhara'i (blocking means to corruption).
3
Analyze the Special Case
Consider when a judge rules against his own ijtihad. By consensus, such a ruling is batin (invalid) for the judge himself. However, the Hanafi school disputes whether it is enforceable (nafidh) externally. Imam Abu Hanifa holds nafidh; the two companions (Sahibayn) hold it should be overturned (naqd).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The text defends the Sahibayn's position.
4
Evaluate the Arguments
The passage presents two objections to the claim that the ruling must be overturned, and then refutes them. The first objection: there is no ijma on non-enforcement because Abu Hanifa himself held nafidh. The second: impermissible acts do not necessarily entail overturning (e.g., divorce during menstruation is valid despite being haram). The response: here the ruling is built on violating one's own ijtihad, which is a prohibited act, leading to corruption (like usurping property), so it must be overturned.
This demonstrates the Hanafi method of 'illa and istidial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: لا ينقض الحكم في الاجتهاديات إذا لم يخالف قاطعاً وهو الكتاب والسنة المتواترة والمشهور والإجماع وفي الهداية: المراد إجماع الأكثر من الصدر الأول وإلا يكن كذلك، بل جاز النقض نقض هذا النقض أيضاً لاجتهاد لاحق ويتسلسل الأمر، فتفوت فائدة نصب الحاكم من فصل الخصومات فإنه لا يتيسر في كل خصومة قاطع يقطع ما وراء مجتهد فيه فيتسلسل الأمر ولو حكم بخلاف اجتهاده كان باطلاً اتفاقاً وإن قلد غيره من المجتهدين يجب عليه العمل بظنه ويحرم اتباع غيره كما مر فإنه ترك لما علمه حكماً إلهياً بما ظنه غير حكم إلهي ولا يجوز له التقليد مع اجتهاده إجماعاً فينقض ما بنى عليه كذا في شرح المختصر، وأورد عليه أن عدم الحل مسلم ولا يلزم منه عدم النفاذ للحكم ونقضه كما عرفت قول الإمام أبي حنيفة وههنا إيرادان: الأول: أن نقل الإجماع ليس في محله فإن الإمام أبا حنيفة قائل بالنفاذ، وهذا الإيراد لأنه حق. والثاني: أنه لا يصح الاستدلال بعدم الحل على عدم النفاذ فإن الشيء لا يحل ولا ينقض، كالطلاق في الحيض، وهذا ليس بشيء، فإن الحكم كان مبنياً على العمل بخلاف الاجتهاد والمبني على الحرام أورث خبثاً فينقض، ولذا حكم الصاحبان بالنقض، وهذا ظاهر جداً في العمد وفي النسيان أيضاً عدم التشبث، وأيضاً في هذا القضاء إعطاء مال أحد للآخر جبراً، ولا سبيل له عليه فهو كالغصب، فينقض القضاء ویرد المال فافهم.
Issue: A ruling is not overturned in matters of ijtihad if it does not contradict a definitive proof, which is the Qur'an, mutawatir and well-known sunna, and consensus. And in al-Hidaya: what is meant is the consensus of the majority of the first generation. Otherwise, if it does, then it is overturned. But overturning this overturning also [occurs] due to a later ijtihad, and the matter would then go on in a chain, and the benefit of appointing a judge in resolving disputes would be lost, because it is not possible in every dispute to have a definitive proof that cuts off what lies behind the matter of ijtihad, so the chain would continue. And if he rules contrary to his own ijtihad, it is invalid by consensus. Even if he follows another mujtahid, he must act according to his own conjecture and it is forbidden for him to follow another, as mentioned, because he would be leaving what he knows as a divine ruling for what he conjectures is not a divine ruling. And it is not permissible for him to do taqlid while he is capable of ijtihad by consensus, so that which is built upon it is overturned. So it is in Sharh al-Mukhtasar. And it was objected that the non-permissibility [of the action] is conceded, but it does not entail the non-enforcement of the ruling or its overturning, as you have known the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa. Here there are two objections: First, the claim of consensus is not in its place, because Imam Abu Hanifa holds enforcement. This objection is correct. Second, it is not valid to infer non-enforcement from non-permissibility, because a thing may be impermissible yet not overturned, like divorce during menstruation. But this is not valid, because the ruling was based on acting contrary to ijtihad, and what is built on the prohibited leads to corruption, so it is overturned. That is why the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) ruled for overturning. This is very clear in the case of intentionality, and also in forgetfulness there is no clinging. Also in this judgment there is compelling payment of one's property to another without right, so it is like usurpation; thus the judgment is overturned and the property is returned. So understand.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage discusses the finality of judicial rulings in matters of ijtihad. The general rule is that if a judge's ruling is based on ijtihad and does not contradict a definitive text (qat'i), it cannot be overturned. If it does contradict a qat'i, it can be overturned. However, overturning it would itself lead to another ijtihad, causing infinite regress. Therefore, the benefit of appointing a judge is lost if every ruling could be overturned. The passage then addresses the case where a judge rules against his own ijtihad. By consensus, such a ruling is invalid. However, Imam Abu Hanifa held that the ruling is nevertheless enforceable (nafidh), while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) held that it should be overturned. The text provides two objections to the claim of consensus: first, Imam Abu Hanifa himself held enforceability, so there is no consensus; second, the argument that impermissible actions cannot be enforced is flawed, as shown by the example of divorce during menstruation (which is impermissible but valid if pronounced). The response is that when a ruling is built on prohibited action, it should be overturned to prevent corruption, as in this case where the judge's ruling would compel the transfer of property unjustly, akin to usurpation.

Key Terms
نقض الحكم (naqd al-hukm): Overturning a court ruling or judgment.
قاطع (qati'): A definitive proof that yields certainty, such as the clear text of Qur'an or mutawatir hadith.
اجتهاديات (ijtihadiyat): Matters subject to ijtihad, where there is no definitive text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can a judge's ruling in ijtihad matters be overturned?
A) Always
B) When it contradicts a qat'i proof
C) Never
D) Only by a higher judge

Key Takeaway
Ijtihad-based court rulings are final and cannot be overturned unless they directly contradict a definitive text from the Qur'an, Mutawatir Sunna, or Ijma al-Salaf.

Change of Ijtihad and the Validity of Past Actions
Branch issue on a mujtahid's marriage without guardian when his ijtihad later changes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that the validity of continuance (baqa') depends on the validity of inception (in'iqad) to determine the status of a mujtahid's past action after a change of ijtihad, and state the effect of a judge's ruling.

Core Idea
A past act based on a valid ijtihad remains valid even if ijtihad changes.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut examines a subtle usul problem: what happens when a mujtahid performs an act (marrying without a guardian) based on his ijtihad, then later changes his ijtihad and believes the act was invalid? The text presents two views and introduces a critical distinction involving a judge's ruling, which illustrates the interplay between personal ijtihad and judicial authority in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the change of ijtihad
The mujtahid married without a guardian, which he initially considered valid. Later his ijtihad changed, and he now believes such a marriage is invalid.
This is a hypothetical used to test the implications of changing ijtihad.
2
Apply the principle of baqa' far' in'iqad
The text states: 'Sihhat al-baqa' far' sihhat al-in'iqad' (the validity of continuance depends on the validity of inception). Since the marriage was validly concluded under his earlier ijtihad, its continuance is valid.
This principle is key to understanding the author's initial reasoning.
3
Consider the objection of complex ignorance
The mujtahid now believes his earlier belief was jahl murakkab (complex ignorance), so he thinks the marriage was actually invalid from the start. Does this override the principle?
Complex ignorance means he was mistaken about the reality, not just the ruling.
4
Contrast with the disbeliever's marriage case
A disbeliever's marriage without witnesses is valid according to his own law and is preserved upon embracing Islam (according to Abu Hanifa). This is because disbelievers were not obligated to follow Islamic rules. The mujtahid, however, was obligated, so his error is more problematic.
This distinction helps clarify the scope of the principle.
5
Recognize the role of a judge's ruling
Some scholars say the marriage remains prohibited unless a judge has ruled on it; in that case, the judicial decision lifts the prohibition and makes it permissible. The author prefers this view.
The judge's ruling effectively resolves the uncertainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرع لو تزوج مجتهد بلا ولي ثم تغير اجتهاده فاختار ابن الحاجب التحريم اتصل به حکم حاكم أم لا لأنه مستديم لما يعتقده حراماً، أقول فيه : أن صحة البقاء فرع صحة الانعقاد وقد كان يعتقد صحته وقت الانعقاد فهو منعقد فكان كنقض الحكم تدبر وفيه أنه وإن كان يعتقد قبل أنه صحيح، لكن الآن اعتقد أن ما كنت زعمت جهل مرکب والنكاح كان فاسداً فيلزم الاستدامة على ما اعتقد أنه حرام من الأصل، وهذا بخلاف نكاح الكافر من غير شهود عند أبي حنيفة، فإنهم لما لم يكونوا مأمورين وكان ذلك جائزاً عندهم فقد انعقد النكاح في نفسه الأمر فلا يفسخ بالإيمان لأنه عاصم، وأما ههنا فقد اعتقد أنه كان مكلفاً بالتعبد بالفساد واعتقاد الصحة جهلاً مركباً، فتأمل ففيه نظر وقيل التحريم إن لم يتصل به حكم حاكم وإلا فالإباحة قال المصنف وهو الأشبه بالصواب لأن القضاء يرفع حكم
Branch: If a mujtahid marries without a guardian, then his ijtihad changes, Ibn al-Hajib chose prohibition regardless of whether a judge's ruling had been connected or not, because he is continuing with what he deems forbidden. I say in it: The validity of continuance depends on the validity of the original conclusion, and he believed it valid at the time of conclusion, so it was validly concluded. So it is like the overturning of a ruling; reflect. And in it is that although he previously believed it valid, now he believes that what I considered was complex ignorance and the marriage was invalid, so continuance on what he believes to be forbidden from the beginning becomes necessary. This is unlike the marriage of a disbeliever without witnesses according to Abu Hanifa, for since they were not commanded and it was permissible in their view, the marriage was valid in itself, so it is not annulled upon embracing Islam because the marriage is preserved. But here, he believes he was obligated to worship the corruption and the belief in validity was complex ignorance. So ponder, for it contains a perspective. And it was said: Prohibition if no judge's ruling was connected, otherwise permissibility. The author said: It is the more similar to correctness, because the judicial decision raises the ruling.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This branch issue deals with a mujtahid who married without a guardian (which he considered valid based on his ijtihad) but later changes his ijtihad and now believes such a marriage is invalid. Ibn al-Hajib holds the marriage remains forbidden (haram) regardless of whether a judge has ruled on it, because he is persisting in what he now deems forbidden. The author discusses that the validity of remaining in the marriage depends on the original validity. Since at the time of contracting the marriage he believed it valid, the contract was validly formed. However, now he believes his previous understanding was mistaken (complex ignorance), so he must consider the marriage invalid from the start and thus cannot continue in it. This is contrasted with a disbeliever's marriage without witnesses: according to Abu Hanifa, since disbelievers are not obligated to follow Islamic marriage rules, their marriage is valid and not annulled upon conversion. Here, the mujtahid believed he was obligated to follow the correct ruling, and his belief in validity was based on error. The text then reports a different view: prohibition unless a judge has passed a ruling on the matter, in which case it becomes permissible. The author (al-Mahbubi? Actually the text says 'the author') considers this latter view more correct because the judge's decision effectively lifts the prohibition.

Key Terms
مجتهد (mujtahid): One qualified to exercise ijtihad.
ولي (wali): Guardian for marriage; in Hanafi law, a woman can contract marriage without a guardian, but some require it.
جهل مركب (jahl murakkab): Complex ignorance: believing something false to be true.
صحة البقاء فرع صحة الانعقاد (sihhat al-baqa' far' sihhat al-in'iqad): The validity of continuance depends on the validity of inception.
حكم حاكم (hukm hakim): A judge's ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the text (said to be 'more similar to correctness'), under which condition does a mujtahid's changed ijtihad not affect the permissibility of his previous marriage?
A) Always, regardless of any condition.
B) Only if no judge has ever ruled on the marriage.
C) Only if a judge has ruled on the marriage (either by validating it or by not intervening).
D) Only if the marriage was witnessed by two Muslims.

Key Takeaway
A past act based on a valid ijtihad remains valid after a change of ijtihad, and a judge's ruling can resolve the uncertainty by lifting the prohibition.

The Hanafi Critique of Tafwid (Delegation of Judgment)
Dispute over the permissibility and occurrence of tafwid (delegation) in Islamic law.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on tafwid, analyze the opposing textual proofs (Quran 3:93 and the hadith of al-idhkhir), and evaluate the Hanafi responses using usul principles.

Core Idea
Tafwid is possible in essence but never occurred; every ruling is based on ijtihad or revelation, not arbitrary choice.

This lesson delves into the classical dispute over tafwid—delegating absolute judgment to a scholar. While the majority of Shafi'is and Malikis consider it rationally permissible, the Hanafi school, following Abu Bakr al-Jassas, argues that tafwid never took place in Islamic law. The debate turns on the interpretation of key Quranic and hadith texts. By tracing the Hanafi responses to these proofs, you will gain insight into how the Hanafi usul framework prioritizes objective rulings based on dalil over subjective delegation.

Guided Path
1
Define tafwid and list the positions
Identify what tafwid means (delegation of judgment) and note the various opinions: Shafi'i/Maliki permissibility, Mu'tazila impermissibility, and Hanafi non-occurrence.
The Hanafi position distinguishes between possibility and actual occurrence.
2
Understand the Hanafi chosen position and its rational basis
Grasp why tafwid is possible in essence but did not occur: the Wise Lawgiver does not delegate rulings to mere choice; the Sharia is bound by ijtihad or taqlid.
The key principle is that rulings are objective, not subjective.
3
Analyze the first opposing proof: Quran 3:93
Examine the verse where Israel prohibited food. The opposition claims this shows delegation. The Hanafi response reinterprets it as ijtihad based on a probable proof (harm).
Consult the proof_chain for a step-by-step usul analysis.
4
Analyze the second opposing proof: hadith of al-idhkhir
The Prophet allowed an exception for al-idhkhir in Mecca. The opposition sees this as choice. The Hanafi response offers multiple interpretations: al-idhkhir is not from fresh grass, the exception is disconnected, or it is abrogation by revelation.
This shows how the Hanafi school skillfully reinterprets texts to uphold objectivity.
5
Evaluate the overall dispute and its implications
Compare the positions and note the thamarah al-khilaf: if tafwid were valid, rulers could arbitrarily change laws. The Hanafi position safeguards the divine nature of rulings.
The chosen view is that tafwid never occurred, according to the majority of Hanafis and other schools.

Question: Is delegation valid, which is that it is said to an alim or mujtahid: 'Judge as you wish, it is correct'? The chosen at most Shafi'is and Malikis and some of us is permissibility rationally. Imam al-Shafi'i hesitated, and upon it is Imam al-Haramayn. And it is said delegation is permitted only for the Prophet, not others. And most Mu'tazila said delegation is not permissible at all, and upon it is Imam Sheikh Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi, and it is the truth, because the ruling is only according to the rational good and evil as passed, and what is good in itself is good, what is evil is evil, so there is no meaning for delegation. Then the chosen among us and among the followers of the three remaining imams is non-occurrence of delegation. For us it is possible in itself, and the principle is to remain as it was, and you are not unaware that possibility is denied. How is it but the same as the claim or equal in ignorance and obviousness? Then we have shown impossibility. As for non-occurrence, it is due to being bound by ijtihad or taqlid, so there remains no place for delegation, following Sheikh Abu Bakr al-Razi. They said: If delegation were allowed, it would lead to the possibility of the absence of the benefit on which the ruling is based, the ignorance of the servant of it, or else it is not so but he rules according to it, then it is ijtihad, not delegation. We say: The lack of his knowledge of it does not necessitate its absence in reality, for perhaps the commander knows that he will choose what contains the benefit, so he delegates to him. And you are not unaware that the reality of delegation is choosing between ruling by it or its opposite, so it is a choice between missing the benefit and not, even if his choice falls on what has benefit. And this choice cannot come from the Wise. Understand the fallers. They said firstly: Allah said: 'Every food was lawful to the Children of Israel except what Israel had made unlawful to himself' (Aal-Imran 93). By choosing to prohibit, he has prohibited. We say: We do not accept that the prohibition was by delegation, but by a probabilistic proof that appeared to him through ijtihad. So he decided upon it and it became a law. Perhaps this proof is that it was harmful to his body, so it was forbidden for him. And it is supported by what Ibn Abbas said: The Jews came and said: O Abu al-Qasim, tell us what Israel had made unlawful to himself? He said: He was living in the desert and suffered from sciatica, and he did not find a cause for his illness except camel meat and milk, so he made them unlawful. They said: You have spoken truth. And they said secondly: He said in the matter of Mecca: 'Its fresh grass is not cut, nor its trees cut.' Then al-Abbas said: Except al-idhkhir, for we put it in our graves. He said: except al-idhkhir. Reported by al-Shaykhan in a long hadith. This is either revelation, or ijtihad, or his choice. There is no revelation nor ijtihad at that moment, so the third is determined. We say: We do not accept that al-idhkhir is from fresh grass, for fresh grass is a thin green plant, while al-idhkhir is a fragrant plant. So the exception is disconnected; its ruling is known by istishab. So its permissibility was categorical and understood before, so it remained. And if it is accepted that al-idhkhir is within fresh grass, we do not accept that he meant it because of the permissibility of specification without exception from before. So the exception is a confirmation of the intended meaning, and it is disconnected from what is mentioned. Yes, it is a connected exception if it is estimated similarly. Then the effort in it is clear, for estimation is necessary, because the speech of two speakers does not relate to each other, nor the speech of one speaker in two times. When estimated, it is a connected exception. As for its disconnection and the confirmation of specification by other than it, a clue is needed. And if we accept generality for al-idhkhir too, then abrogation is allowed, meaning it may be abrogation by revelation in the blink of an eye, especially in the view of the Hanafis that his inspiration is revelation. This is the truth in the answer. If it is said: The exception contradicts abrogation, for it prevents the ruling from the beginning, and abrogation brings it then removes it. We say: The exception is from what is estimated in the speech of al-Abbas, or from what is estimated in his speech secondly, not from what he mentioned, for it is absolutely general, then the ruling of some of its individuals is abrogated. I say: So on this, al-Abbas's exception is in exchange for the text, and that is based on the permissibility of specification by ijtihad. Ponder. This is not anything, for al-Abbas's intent was to ask for the exception of al-idhkhir, because needs depend on it like burying the dead and building houses. So Allah answered his supplication and abrogated His ruling. So the meaning of his saying: 'O Messenger of Allah, except al-idhkhir, O Messenger of Allah, make the entire fresh grass forbidden except al-idhkhir,' from the generality of specification in something. Understand. And they said thirdly: The Messenger of Allah said: 'If I did not fear burdening my nation, I would have ordered them to use the siwak,' and it has preceded. And the saying of al-Aqra' ibn Habis: 'Is this Hajj for our year or forever?' He said: 'Forever, and if I had said yes, it would have become obligatory.' This is obvious in choice. And the saying that it is a conditional hypothetical report about the necessity of the other impossible is far, because custom uses it for choice. And when al-Nadr ibn al-Harith was killed in captivity, and he was the most wretched of the disbelievers and was fiercely hostile to the Messenger of Allah, Allah enabled him to kill him. He heard what his daughter and his sister Qutayla recited: 'O Muhammad, for you are a noble derivative, in your people, and the stallion is deep-rooted.' He said: 'If I had heard it before his killing, I would have shown mercy to him.' This is obvious in choice. We say: We do not accept that the mentioned things indicate choice; rather it is possible that revelation was so, thus no choice.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage addresses the question of tafwid (delegation): whether it is valid to tell a scholar or mujtahid 'judge as you wish, it is correct.' The author presents multiple opinions: most Shafi'is and Malikis, and some Hanafis, allow it rationally; Imam al-Shafi'i hesitated; some say it is only for the Prophet; most Mu'tazila deny it absolutely, and Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi holds it is false because rulings are objective based on rational good and evil. The chosen Hanafi position (along with the other three schools) is that tafwid is possible in itself but did not occur in the Sharia. The reasoning: possibility is there in essence, but the fact that we are bound by ijtihad or taqlid leaves no room for delegation. The author then responds to opponents' arguments. The first proof from the Quran: 'Every food was lawful to the Children of Israel except what Israel had made unlawful to himself.' Opponents say this shows Israel chose to prohibit via delegation. The Hanafi response: the prohibition was not by delegation but by a probable proof that appeared to him through ijtihad, supported by Ibn Abbas' explanation that it was due to harm to his body. The second proof from the hadith about Mecca: the Prophet said 'do not cut its fresh grass or trees,' and al-Abbas asked for an exception for al-idhkhir, which the Prophet allowed. Opponents say this shows the Prophet exercised personal choice, not revelation or ijtihad. The Hanafi response offers several interpretations: (a) al-idhkhir is not from fresh grass, so the exception is disconnected; (b) even if it is, the exception is a confirmation of the intended meaning or was based on a prior specification; (c) if generality is accepted, then it may be abrogation by instantaneous revelation. The third proof from the hadith about siwak and the story of al-Aqra' ibn Habis and al-Nadr: these show the Prophet's choice. The Hanafi reply: these do not definitely indicate choice; they could be based on revelation. The overall conclusion is that tafwid is not a valid institution in the Sharia, and the arguments for it are either misinterpreted or based on insufficient evidence.

Key Terms
تفويض (tafwid): Delegation: telling a scholar or mujtahid to judge as he wishes, and his judgment is considered correct

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the chosen Hanafi position on tafwid (delegation)?
A) It is permissible and occurred.
B) It is possible but did not occur in the Sharia.
C) It is completely impermissible.
D) It is only for the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
Tafwid (delegation) is not a valid institution in Hanafi usul; every Islamic ruling is grounded in objective proof (dalil) or authoritative guidance (ijtihad/taqlid).

Ijtihad — Independent Reasoning
advanced
8 min
Permissibility of an Era Without a Mujtahid (Khulu al-Zaman 'an al-Mujtahid)
Arguing that a time devoid of mujtahids is legally permissible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on khulu al-zaman 'an al-mujtahid, identify the key proof from the hadith of Bukhari, and evaluate the Hanbali counter-argument using the hadith of the 'ta'ifah zahirah'.

Core Idea
An era without a mujtahid is legally permissible according to Hanafis, contrary to Hanbalis, based on the hadith of knowledge being taken away.

In this usul al-fiqh passage, we explore a classical dispute: can there be a time when no qualified mujtahid exists? The Hanafis argue yes, using a prophetic hadith that describes a future without scholars. The Hanbalis object, citing another hadith about a continuous group upholding the truth. The commentator refines the arguments, clarifying the scope of the dispute and critiquing certain claims. This lesson will guide you through the reasoning and the thamarah al-khilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mas'ala and Opposing Schools
Read the opening sentence to grasp the issue: 'يجوز خلو الزمان عن المجتهد شرعاً' (it is permissible for an era to be devoid of a mujtahid legally). Note the opposing schools: Hanbalis and al-Isnad. Understand that the dispute is specifically about the period before the major signs of the Hour.
The text clarifies that after the signs, absence is agreed upon. Jesus (alayhi al-salam) is an exception as he rules by divine inspiration.
2
Locate the Hanafi Proof and Analyze its Dalala
Find the Hanafi dalil: the hadith from Bukhari stating that knowledge is taken away by the death of scholars until no scholar remains. Identify the operative phrase 'حتى إذا لم يبق عالم' (until no scholar remains). Classify the hadith as ahad (zanni al-thubut) and its dalala as zanni, but it strongly implies a time without scholars, hence without mujtahids.
The commentator (أقول) notes that the hadith proves absence of any scholar, but the dispute is about absence of a mujtahid before the signs; thus the proof is not directly on point.
3
Examine the Hanbali Proof and the Hanafi Response
The Hanbalis cite the hadith: 'لا تزال طائفة من أمتي ظاهرين على الحق...' (a group will continue manifest upon the truth). Understand their argument: this implies a continuous existence of those capable of ijtihad. The Hanafi response: the hadith only indicates that such a group exists at times, not that it must exist at every moment. Absence is still possible.
The Hanbali counter-reply: if absence were possible, it would imply the Shari'ah could be false (God forbid), so it must be prevented. The commentator seems to side with the Hanafi position by arguing that the hadith of continuous group actually shows obligation in reality.
4
Understand the Thamarah al-Khilaf and Conclusion
The practical consequence: if absence is permissible, then in times with no mujtahid, laymen must perform taqlid of a madhhab. If not permissible, there must always be a living mujtahid to consult. The Hanafi view allows for taqlid in such scenarios.
The passage ends by dismissing those who claimed ijtihad ended with al-Nasafi or the four imams, branding them as misguided.

هوساتهم لم يأتوا بدليل ولا يعبأ بكلامهم وإنما هم من الذين حكم الحديث أنهم أفتوا بغير علم فضلوا وأضلوا ولم يفهموا أن هذا إخبار بالغيب في خمس لا يعلمهن إلا الله تعالى، الحنابلة (قالوا : أولاً : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم (لا يزال طائفة من أمتي ظاهرين على الحق حتى يأتي أمر الله أو حتى يظهر الدجال أو حتى يقاتل آخر هذه الأمة الدجال (وأجيب بأنه غاية ما لزم منه عدم وقوع النفي لكن لا يدل على نفي الجواز (له فإن أحد الجائزين بما لا يقع ورد بأنه يلزم منه الامتناع شرعاً وإلا لزم كذبه أي الشرع العياذ بالله، والنزاع إنما وقع فيه أقول : على أن الدوام لا يخلو عن ضرورة) في الواقع ولو غيرته، وإذ قد دل الدليل على الوقوع الدائمي فلزم الوجوب قطعاً ولو بالغير، وإن تأملت حق التأمل
Issue: It is permissible for an era to be devoid of a mujtahid, according to the Sharia, contrary to the Hanbalis and al-Isnad. For they do not permit it according to the Sharia, though they allow it rationally. The dispute is only concerning the period before the signs of the Hour: the emergence of the Dajjal, Gog and Magog, the Beast of the Earth, and the rising of the sun from the west. As for the absence after the appearance of the signs of the Hour, it is agreed upon. As for the gathering of Jesus (peace be upon him), even though he enters into the Muhammadan religion, the reality is that he gives fatwa by divine inspiration; falsehood cannot come from before him or behind him. He judges an incident in the Muhammadan religion as such; he judges by it, not through ijtihad. And the dispute is concerning the absolute mujtahid, whether he is a mujtahid within the madhhab or a mujtahid in the madhhab. That is what is meant when speaking of an era devoid of an absolute mujtahid, definitely, as explicitly stated by Imam al-Ghazali, al-Qaffal, and al-Rafi'i. In al-Khulasa: 'There is no one from the people of ijtihad in our time.' And because what necessarily follows from the evidences of the two groups is either the existence of an absolute mujtahid or its negation. Thus in al-Hashiya. Our proof: The saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family): 'Indeed, Allah does not take away knowledge by snatching it from the servants, but He takes away knowledge by taking away the scholars, until when no scholar remains, the people take ignorant leaders, and they give fatwa without knowledge, so they go astray and lead others astray.' Reported by Bukhari. This indicates that no scholar remains on earth at that time. I say: There is something in this. Because the most that follows from it is an era devoid of a scholar, but the dispute is concerning an era devoid before the occurrence of the signs of the Hour. So what is necessitated is other than what is claimed, and what is claimed is not necessitated. Ponder. Then he argued with what Imam Hujjat al-Islam (may Allah sanctify his soul), al-Rafi'i, and al-Qaffal explicitly stated: that this absence has occurred in our time. There is something in that, because the occurrence of absence is denied, and what was mentioned is merely a claim. And Imam Hujjat al-Islam, though he is among the saints, is not a valid proof in ijtihadi matters. Then among the people are those who ruled the obligation of absence after 'Allamah al-Nasafi and that ijtihad ended with him, and they meant ijtihad within the madhhab. As for absolute ijtihad, they said it ended with the four imams, to the extent that they made it obligatory for the community to follow one of these four? All of this is their foolishness; they brought no proof, and their words are not considered. Rather, they are among those whom the hadith ruled: they gave fatwa without knowledge, so they went astray and led others astray. They did not understand that this is news of the unseen, of the five things that none knows except Allah. The Hanbalis said: First: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family) said: 'A group of my community will continue to be manifest upon the truth until the command of Allah comes, or until the Dajjal appears, or until the last of this community fights the Dajjal.' And it was replied: The most that follows from it is that negation does not occur, but it does not indicate the negation of permissibility, because one of two permissible things may not occur. To which it was responded: That would necessarily entail legal prevention, otherwise it would entail a lie from the Shari'ah (God forbid!). The dispute is only concerning its occurrence. I say: Continuity is not free from necessity in reality, even if it were altered. And when the proof indicates permanent occurrence, then obligation necessarily follows, even if through another. If you truly ponder.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is a mas'ala (issue) in usul al-fiqh regarding the permissibility of an era being devoid of a mujtahid according to the Shari'ah. The Hanafi position, as presented here, is that such an absence is legally permissible, contrary to the Hanbalis and others (al-Isnad). The dispute is specifically about the period before the major signs of the Hour (ashrat al-sa'ah). After those signs appear, absence is agreed upon. Jesus (alayhi al-salam) is an exception; he gives rulings by divine inspiration, not ijtihad. The term 'mujtahid' here includes both a mujtahid within the madhhab and an absolute mujtahid, as clarified by Imam al-Ghazali, al-Qaffal, and al-Rafi'i. The Hanafi proof is the hadith from Bukhari that knowledge is taken away by the death of scholars, leading to ignorant leaders giving fatwa without knowledge. This implies an era without scholars. The commentator (Mulla Nizam al-Din al-Ansari?) adds a note: the hadith indicates an era devoid of any scholar, but the dispute is about before the signs, so the hadith does not directly address the disputed case. He also critiques the appeal to the authority of Imam al-Ghazali, stating his claim is not a proof in ijtihad. The Hanbalis argue using the hadith of the continuous group manifest upon the truth. The Hanafi response is that this only proves that such a group exists sometimes, not that it must exist always. The Hanbalis counter that if it were not necessary, it would imply the possibility of the Shari'ah being false, which is impossible. The commentator seems to side with the Hanafi view that the hadith indicates permanent occurrence, making it obligatory in practice, but the overall Hanafi position is still that absence is possible by intellectual reasoning, though the hadith shows it may not occur. The passage ends with a warning about those who claim ijtihad ended with al-Nasafi or the four imams, dismissing them as misguided.

Key Terms
المجتهد المطلق (al-mujtahid al-mutlaq): A scholar who is capable of deriving rulings directly from the primary sources without being bound to a specific madhhab.
خلو الزمان عن المجتهد (khulu al-zaman 'an al-mujtahid): A period in history where no living scholar meets the qualifications of ijtihad according to the Shari'ah.
طائفة ظاهرة على الحق (ta'ifah zahirah 'ala al-haqq): The group mentioned in the hadith that will continue to be manifest upon the truth. Its existence is used by Hanbalis to argue for the continuity of mujtahids.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this mas'ala, what is the ruling on an era being devoid of a mujtahid?
A) It is impossible legally and rationally.
B) It is permissible legally, though it may not occur.
C) It is obligatory for there to be a mujtahid at all times.
D) It is permissible only after the signs of the Hour.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafis allow for an era without a mujtahid, grounding their view in the hadith of the gradual loss of knowledge, and they respond to the Hanbali counter-proof by distinguishing between actual existence and necessary existence.

8 min
The Permissibility of an Era Without a Mujtahid: Hanafi vs Hanbali
Dispute between Hanafis and Hanbalis on whether an era can be devoid of a mujtahid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the permissibility of an era without a mujtahid, explain the Hanbali objection, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
An era can lack a mujtahid legally; Hanafis argue from the hadith of removal of scholars.

The question of whether an era can be devoid of a qualified mujtahid is a foundational usul dispute between the Hanafi and Hanbali schools. This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut presents the arguments of both sides, with the Hanafi position supported by a well-known hadith. Understanding this khilaf clarifies the epistemological status of ijtihad across time and the validity of taqlid of earlier mujtahids.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed claim
State exactly what the Hanafis permit and the Hanbalis reject: the legal permissibility of an era with no mujtahid (absolute or within a madhhab).
The dispute is before the major signs of the Hour.
2
Extract the Hanafi dalil
Find the hadith quoted by the Hanafis: 'Allah does not take away knowledge by snatching it... but by taking away the scholars, until when no scholar remains...' Explain how it implies a time without a mujtahid.
The hadith is from Bukhari.
3
Analyze the Hanbali counter-arguments
Two objections: 1) The hadith 'a group will remain on the truth' suggests continuous mujtahids. 2) Ijtihad is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) in every age because new events require rulings.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The author replies: 1) The hadith guarantees continuity of the truth, not of mujtahids. 2) Partial mujtahids or reliance on past rulings can fulfill the obligation. The practical consequence: Hanafis allow following deceased mujtahids.
The text sides with the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاتمة في الاجتهاد والتقليد أصلا (أو خير فيها) تخييرا معينا، أقول ولا يلزم منه وقوع التفويض كما توهم ابن الهمام لأنه سلم التخيير في الحكم لأن التخيير معين من الحكم وهو الإباحة في الفعل والترك، والتفويض تخيير في تعيين، وليس فيه شيء من حكم معين فتأمل فإنه دقيق) ولا يذهب عليك أنه صحيح في الصورة الأخيرة، وأما الصورتان السابقتان فصحته فيهما لا تخلو عن كلفة، ويلزم فيه إلزام الشيخ فتأمل. (مسألة): يجوز خلو الزمان عن المجتهد شرعا خلافا للحنابلة والإسناد) فإنهم لا يجوزونه شرعا وإن جاز عقلا (والنزاع) إنما هو فيما قبل أشراط الساعة من خروج الدجال ويأجوج ومأجوج، ودابة الأرض، وطلوع الشمس من المغرب، فالخلو بعد ظهور أشراط الساعة عليه، وأما مجمع عيسى عليه السلام فهو وإن كان يدخل في الدين المحمدي لكن التحقيق أنه يفتي بإلهام إلهي لا يأتيه الباطل من بين يديه ولا من خلفه، أن حكم حكم الحادثة في الدين المحمدي كذا، فيحكم به لا عن اجتهاد (و) النزاع (في المجتهد مطلقا) سواء كان مجتهدا في المذهب أو مجتهدا بالمذهب. وهو المراد إذا أطلق لخلو الزمان عن المجتهد المطلق قطعا كما صرح به الإمام الغزالي والقفال والرافعي وفي «الخلاصة»، ليس أحد من أهل الاجتهاد في زماننا، ولأن اللازم من دلائل الفريقين ثبوت المجتهد مطلقا أو انتفاؤه، كذا في «الحاشية» (لنا) قوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم: (إن الله لا يقبض العلم انتزاعا ينتزعه من العباد، لكن يقبض العلم بقبض العلماء، حتى إذا لم يبق عالم اتخذ الناس رؤساء جهالا فأفتوا بغير علم فضلوا وأضلوا) رواه البخاري وهذا يدل على عدم بقاء عالم في الأرض في زمان (أقول: فيه ما فيه لأن غاية ما يلزم منه خلو الزمان عن العالم، والنزاع إنما وقع في خلوه قبل وقوع أشراط الساعة، فما لزم غير المدعي وما هو مدعي غير لازم ( فتأمل) ثم إنه استدل بما صرح به الإمام حجة الإسلام قدس سره الرافعي والقفال بأنه وقع في زماننا هذا الخلو، وفيه ما فيه، لأن وقوع الخلو ممنوع، وما ذكر مجرد دعوى والإمام حجة الإسلام وإن كان من الأولياء لا يصلح حجة في الاجتهاديات، ثم إن من الناس من حكم بوجوب الخلو من بعد العلامة النسفي واختتم الاجتهاد به وعنوا الاجتهاد في المذهب وأما الاجتهاد المطلق فقالوا: أختتم بالأئمة الأربعة حتى أوجبوا تقليد واحد من هؤلاء على الأمة؟ وهذا كله هوساتهم لم يأتوا بدليل ولا يعبأ بكلامهم وإنما هم من الذين حكم الحديث أنهم أفتوا بغير علم فضلوا وأضلوا ولم يفهموا أن هذا إخبار بالغيب في خمس لا يعلمهن إلا الله تعالى، الحنابلة (قالوا: أولا: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم (لا يزال طائفة من أمتي ظاهرين على الحق حتى يأتي أمر الله أو حتى يظهر الدجال أو حتى يقاتل آخر هذه الأمة الدجال (وأجيب بأنه غاية ما لزم منه عدم وقوع النفي لكن لا يدل على نفي الجواز (له فإن أحد الجائزين بما لا يقع ورد بأنه يلزم منه الامتناع شرعا وإلا لزم كذبه أي الشرع العياذ بالله، والنزاع إنما وقع فيه أقول: على أن الدوام لا يخلو عن ضرورة) في الواقع ولو غيرته، وإذ قد دل الدليل على الوقوع الدائمي فلزم الوجوب قطعا ولو بالغير، وإن تأملت حق التأمل وجدت هذه العلاوة مغايرة لما تقدم، وإذا لم يتم الجواب المذكور (فالوجه) في الجواب (أن اللازم من دليلكم دوام اعتقاد الحق لا دوام وقوع (الاجتهاد والمطلوب هذا دون ذلك (و) قالوا: (ثانيا: الاجتهاد فرض كفاية) في كل عصر (لأن الحوادث غير متناهية، فلا يكفي تقليد (الميت لأنه ما بين حكم الحادثة التي حدثت بعده (فلو خلا) عصر عنه (اجتمعوا على الباطل) وهو باطل بالشرع والجواب الملازمة ممنوعة فإن الخلو عن المجتهد المطلق لا يلزم منه الإجماع على الباطل لجواز أن يوجد في كل عصر مجتهد في المذهب أو مجتهد في البعض، و (الجواب) ثانيا إذا فرض موت العلماء فالبطلان للتالي ممنوع لأن المبادىء شرط) ومن جملتها العلماء، واجتماع العلماء لا يكون على باطل لا مطلقا فتدبر) وفيه شيء، فإنه يلزم منه أن يعمل كل الأمة بالباطل، فلم يكونوا على الحق، فالأولى أن يقال إنه لا يلزم الاجتماع على الباطل، وإنما لو ابتلي كل أحد بالحادثة الجديدة التي لم يستخرج حكمها المجتهدون السابقون وهو ممنوع فافهم.
Conclusion on ijtihad and taqlid originally... (Issue): It is permissible for an era to be devoid of a mujtahid legally, contrary to the Hanbalis and al-Isnad. For they do not permit it legally although it is permissible rationally. The dispute is only concerning before the signs of the Hour... Our proof: His saying (PBUH): 'Indeed Allah does not take away knowledge by snatching it from the servants, but He takes away knowledge by taking away the scholars, until when no scholar remains, people take ignorant leaders, they give fatwa without knowledge, and they go astray and lead astray.' Reported by Bukhari... The Hanbalis said: First: The Messenger of Allah (PBUH) said: 'A group of my community will continue to be manifest upon the truth until the command of Allah comes or until the Dajjal appears...' It is answered that... Second: Ijtihad is a communal obligation in every age because accidents are infinite... The answer: The required connection is denied...
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This is a usul dispute on whether an era can be legally empty of a mujtahid. The Hanafi position permits it, based on a hadith indicating that scholars will be taken away until no scholar remains. The Hanbalis object, citing the hadith that a group will remain on the truth, and argue that ijtihad is a communal obligation. The commentator rebuts that the hadith only guarantees the continued existence of the truth, not of mujtahids, and that the obligation of ijtihad can be fulfilled by partial mujtahids or by following earlier rulings. The passage also clarifies that the dispute concerns the period before the major signs of the Hour, and that Jesus (AS) rules by divine inspiration, not ijtihad.

Key Terms
خلو الزمان عن المجتهد (khuluww al-zaman 'an al-mujtahid): A period in which no qualified mujtahid (absolute or within a madhhab) exists.
مجتهد مطلق (mujtahid mutlaq): An absolute mujtahid who can derive rulings directly from primary sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, is it legally permissible for an era to be devoid of any mujtahid?
A) Yes, it is permissible
B) No, it is not permissible
C) It is permissible only before the Day of Judgment
D) It is permissible but sinful

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits an era without a mujtahid; the primary proof is the hadith of the removal of scholars, and the Hanbali objections are answered by distinguishing between the truth and the institution of ijtihad.
